It is subjective to assume that what God ]{.class_s1T0}[did ]{.class_s1T2-1}[]{#cF7.xhtml_page_70}[with the Byzantine type text has no relation to the ]{.class_s1T0}[quality ]{.class_s1T2-1}[of that text. It is subjective to say that the Bible is like any other book. It is subjective to assume God allowed the truth to be hidden until the recovery of a Roman Catholic manuscript in 1885!]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a23P}[\[238\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1TW){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ And it is very subjective to presume that God doesn't know ]{.class_s1T0}[the motives ]{.class_s1T2-1}[of translators and revisers.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a279}[\[239\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1TX){.class_s1T7 .noteref}

Materials for reconstructing a Greek New Testament consist of:

1. The uncial manuscripts. (Codices and vellum scrolls written in block capital Greek letters.)

2. The cursives. (Referred to sometimes as "minuscules," lower case Greek writings, as with a flowing motion.)

3. The lectionaries. (Service books for church worship which would be similar to the "responsive readings" in the back of some modern hymnals. These writings contain Scripture "lessons" or "readings.")

4. The Church Fathers. (These are the Christians who left works in writing after the close of the canon. They may be classified as Alexandrian, Eastern, and Western, or Ante-Nicene, Post-Nicene, etc.)

5. Early translations. (These are translations of the Greek New Testament into other languages such as Syriac, Old Latin, Coptic, etc.)

[6. The papyrus fragments. (Small scraps of paper, or occasionally several pages, on perishable paper; they include many writings that have nothing to do with the Bible]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2MM}[\[240\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1UJ){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ as well as portions of Scripture.)]{.class_s1T0}

7. Conjectures of scholars. (These are the least valuable and amount to practically nothing when one considers that 95 percent of the scholars got off on the wrong foot when they consented to "pocketing their convictions" for the sake of finding "the originals." If the "originals" were written by men who had convictions like [Peter, James, and Paul (!), ]{.class_s1T2-0}how would a [neutral scholar EVER recover them? ]{.class_s1T2-0}\[You see, the whole approach is fantastic.\])

8. Sermons of early preachers. (Citations from sermons []{#cF7.xhtml_page_71}preached or written around A.D. 200--400 furnish some evidence for the condition of the text at that time.)

I. The Greek Uncial Manuscripts.

[These comprise 140 copies, dating from the fourth to the tenth century.]{.class_s206}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a285}[\[241\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2BR){.class_s284 .noteref}[ Recently, about seventy-two more uncial manuscripts have showed up.]{.class_s206}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a287}[\[242\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2BS){.class_s284 .noteref}[ The one most "universally esteemed" in this group is the Roman Catholic Vaticanus, titled "B" in the critical apparatus of Greek Testaments. (The notation for the Jehovah's Witness' Bible, ]{.class_s206}[New World Translation,]{.class_s207-1}[ is "1209")]{.class_s206}

[Vaticanus popped up in the Vatican library in 1481. It was written around A.D. 350--370, and it survived eleven centuries in excellent condition, due to the fact that the Christians never used it.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2EF}[\[243\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a27B){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ Its reading in John 1:18, μονογενης θεος (a "neutral" text?!), showed every Christian exactly what it was---a Gnostic depravation.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a1TM}[\[244\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a27C){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ The manuscript is written on fine vellum (tanned animal skins), and it has 759 pages, 10 inches by 10½ inches, each containing three narrow columns of about forty-one lines to the column.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a26C}[\[245\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a27D){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ It contains the Epistle to Barnabas and the Apocrypha.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a1V1}[\[246\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a27E){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ Vaticanus was written by the same man as Sinaiticus (according to Tishendorf),]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a1Z5}[\[247\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a27F){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ but the Pope insists that his manuscript must be earlier than Sinaiticus (Aleph) because of the way that the divisions are placed in the Gospels.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2HA}[\[248\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a27G){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ The Vatican manuscript omits Genesis 1:1 through Genesis 46:28; Psalms 106 through Psalms 138; Matthew 16:2--3; Romans 16:24; the Pauline Pastoral Epistles; Revelation; and everything in Hebrews after Hebrews 9:14. This convenient dissection speaks worlds for its authors and its preservers; for, marvel of marvels, here is a vellum manuscript that can survive sixteen centuries with what scholars call "the best text," "the most perfectly preserved text," "a remarkable pure text," "beautifully preserved text," "highly legible," etc., and yet it takes off ]{.class_s1T0}[the front of the Bible (Genesis), the middle of the Bible (Psalms), the end of the Bible (Revelation), ]{.class_s1T2-1}[and then drops the chapter in Hebrews that deals with ]{.class_s1T0}[the one, eternal effectual sacrifice of Jesus Christ which did away with the "sacraments"!]{.class_s1T2-1}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a1WF}[\[249\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a27H){.class_s1TN .noteref}

(Westcott and Hort are really "neutral," are they not, in their approach to the "original text"?)

[According to Westcott and Hort, Vaticanus was written in Italy, where the Isidorian Decretals and the Donation of Constantine]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a272}[\[250\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2CH){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ were written. ]{.class_s1T0}[Is this a good place to look for a "pure" text?]{.class_s1T2-1}

The Vatican manuscript was available at the time of the translation of the [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611 and was even referred to by Erasmus in 1515 and he ignored it.[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2NA .class-0}[\[251\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2MJ){.class_s1SX .noteref} Why shouldn't he? What would any man do with "Vaticanus" (Humanist, Rationalist, Communist, Atheist, Catholic, Protestant, or Jew) if his purpose was to print a New Testament Greek text which was cherished by [New Testament Christians? ]{.class_s1SV-0}Would he accept a manuscript that changed ΘΕΟΣ ΕΦΑΝΕΡΩΘΗ ΕΝ ΣΑΡΚΙ [("God was manifest in the flesh")]{.class_s1SW-0} to ΟΣ ΕΦΑΝΕΡΩΘΗ ΕΝ ΣΑΡΚΙ ("who was manifested in the flesh")? (See 1 Tim. 3:16.) The thing is incredible, for ΟΣ has no antecedent in the first part of the verse! ΤΟ ΜΥΣΤΗΡΙΟΝ is neuter, not masculine! Observe how the [ASV ]{.class_s1SV-0}(1901) and the [RSV ]{.class_s1SV-0}(1952) picked up this Vatican reading without batting an eye. While doing this, their revision committees were clouding the eyes of the Christians with a fog of verbiage to the effect that the [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611 had "archaic words" which must be "brought up-to-date"! Wouldn't it be good to learn how to read one syllable neuter and masculine words before one undertook to be the pedagogue of people who can already read and understand them?

[Vaticanus ("B") was called by Westcott and Hort a "neutral text preserved on an island of purity." (How Italy fits this description is a little difficult to see; consequently, modern scholars have abandoned the theory that Vaticanus was written there. They have also abandoned the idea that it was written by Eusebius \[in Caesarea\] or that anyone copied it from Eusebius.) Vaticanus has been assigned to the limbo of lost authors: the presbyter John, the Q Document of Matthew, the Second Isaiah, and Deuter-dumpty (see ]{.class_s1T0}[Bible Believer's Commentary on Genesis]{.class_s1T2-1}[---Gen. 16:13). Among scores of fatalities, errors, and outright inanities, the Vatican manuscript exhibits the belly dancer of Mark 6:22 as ]{.class_s1T0}[Herod's own daughter!]{.class_s1T2-1}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2KG}[\[252\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a24E){.class_s1TN .noteref}[ (Not even Goodspeed \[1923\], a rank Liberal, could "stomach" that one!)]{.class_s1T0}

We shall study Vaticanus in much more detail in the next []{#cF7.xhtml_page_73}chapter.

Sinaticus is the next Greek uncial manuscript which deserves our attention. It is designated by the Hebrew letter Aleph (`<bdi dir="rtl">`{=html}א`</bdi>`{=html}) in the critical apparatus of Greek Testaments, and its present home is London, England.

[This manuscript, as Vaticanus, is on vellum, although it is a thinner vellum than Vaticanus.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2BW}[\[253\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a24F){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ It is the only uncial manuscript containing all of the New Testament (according to the "majority of scholars"). It also throws the "Shepherd of Hermas" and the "Epistle of Barnabas" into the New Testament, and originally]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a29R}[\[254\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a24G){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ it contained part of the "Didache." It was written about A.D. 350--370 on 147½ leaves of vellum, in four columns of fourty-eight lines each to the page.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2CK}[\[255\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a24H){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ The pages are 15 inches by 13½ inches.]{.class_s1T0}

[Westcott and Hort aided the Pope in suggesting that Sinaiticus was NOT written as early as Vaticanus, nor was it transcribed by the same writer. The Sinaitic manuscript was found in St. Catherine's monastery on Mr. Sinai by Tischendorf, and the man who gave him the "lead" on it referred to it as ]{.class_s1T0}["The Septuagint"!]{.class_s1T2-1}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a1Z4}[\[256\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1Z8){.class_s1TN .noteref}[ That is, this man (who was a monk) accepted it ]{.class_s1T0}[as fact ]{.class_s1T2-1}[that Origen's Hexapla and subsequent revisions were written 200 B.C.---]{.class_s1T0}[which they were NOT.]{.class_s1T2-1}

[When the scholars say that Sinaiticus contains the "complete New Testament," they tell you a lie. What they mean is, "It contains all of the New Testament except John 5:4, 8:1--11; Matthew 16:2--3; Romans 16:24; Mark 16:9--20; 1 John 5:7; Acts 8:37 and a dozen other verses." Sinaiticus, as Vaticanus, has survived the storms of the centuries because it was in a monastery; and who in the world in a Greek Orthodox or Roman monastery ever used the Bible for soul winning and personal work? (Patrick \[389--461\], Columban \[543--615\], and Martin Luther \[1483--1546\] did; but they used the Old Latin and the Greek of Erasmus, ]{.class_s1T0}[not the revised Latin of Jerome and the Greek of Origen.]{.class_s1T2-1}[)]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2AU}[\[257\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2KW){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ Origen's "Septuagint" doesn't seem to produce any ]{.class_s1T0}[results ]{.class_s1T2-1}[in the lives of those who study, buy, and sell it.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a20M}[\[258\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2KX){.class_s1T7 .noteref}

[Very often Sinaiticus will agree with the readings of the ]{.class_s1T0}[AV ]{.class_s1T2-1}[1611 against the readings of Vaticanus, but on the whole, the scribe has relied heavily on North African scholarship for the correct text]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a1ZZ}[\[259\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a263){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ []{#cF7.xhtml_page_74}and has paid very little attention to the Holy Spirit or the Holy Bible.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a27N}[\[260\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a264){.class_s1T7 .noteref}

[The third uncial manuscript to take note of is "Alexandrinus" (noted in the critical markings as "A"). It is written on 773 leaves of vellum of about 10]{.class_s1T0}[3]{.class_s1T7}[/]{.class_s1T0}[8]{.class_s1WM}[ inches by 12]{.class_s1T0}[5]{.class_s1T7}[/]{.class_s1T0}[8]{.class_s1WM}[ inches, with two columns of Scriptures running forty-one lines to the page.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a288}[\[261\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1WN){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ It omits John 6:50 through 8:52; 2 Corinthians 4:13 through 12:6; 1 Kings 12:20 through14:9; Matthew 1:1 through 25:6; Genesis 15:1--5; Genesis 14:14--17; and Genesis chapters 16--19. It contains the remnants of the two epistles of Clement (supposedly A.D. 95 and A.D. 100).]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2BM}[\[262\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1WP){.class_s1T7 .noteref}

Manuscript "A" (written in the fifth century) bears a strong resemblance to the Byzantine text of the [AV ]{.class_s1T2-0}1611, and it must never be forgotten that any set of manuscripts (genuine or counterfeit) must contain 90 percent of the [AV ]{.class_s1T2-0}1611 text in order to pass off as "Bibles."

There are other uncial manuscripts, but these need only the briefest mention, for the majority of uncial manuscripts will bear witness to the [AV ]{.class_s1T2-0}1611 text time and time again, and even "B," Aleph, and "A" must go along to keep up with the pack.

[There is "C" (Codex Ephremi Rescriptus), a fifth century "twice written" manuscript which was brought to Italy in the sixteenth century.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a26K}[\[263\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2KD){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ There is Codex "D" (Bezae Cantabrigiensis), a fifth century uncial manuscript now at Cambridge.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a259}[\[264\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2KE){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ There is "W" (Codex Washingtoniensis), a fourth century manuscript which bears a strong witness to the AV 1611 readings. In addition to these will be found "E," "F," "G," "H," "K," etc., and right on down the line, manuscripts written in block capital Greek letters. A list can be found in any edition of Nestle's after 1952.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2B2}[\[265\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2KF){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ Uncial manuscripts are found in the tenth and eleventh centuries ("H" Seidelianus II, "K" Cyprius, "X" Freerianus, "H" Mutinensis, etc.).]{.class_s1T0}

The uncial manuscripts run from A through Z with the omission of any manuscript "J," "R," or "Z." Nine Greek letters have been adopted for manuscripts from the sixth to the tenth century: Γ, Δ, Θ, Λ, Ξ, Π, Σ, Φ, and Ψ.

There are many other uncial fragments which are seldom cited because they agree with the Receptus so many times that it is []{#cF7.xhtml_page_75}embarrassing for the advocates of the Westcott and Hort theory to list them. They are usually listed by numbers such as 046, 047, 048, 049, 050, 051, etc., up to numbers as high as 0250.

II\. The Greek Cursives.

[These are manuscripts using lower case letters which make up the texts; they are referred to as "minuscules" in distinction from "majuscules" (uncials).]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a28U}[\[266\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a234){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ These number about 2,429 manuscripts]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a1YD}[\[267\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a235){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ dating from the ninth to the sixteenth century. In Nestle's critical apparatus they are listed by thin, slanting numbers.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a205}[\[268\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a236){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ They make up the vast majority of New Testament manuscripts and bear witness (99 percent of the time) to the text of the ]{.class_s1T0}[AV ]{.class_s1T2-1}[1611. The cursive style is the style adopted by all of the critical Greek editions (Nestle, 1898; Alford, 1849; Westcott and Hort, 1881; Tischendorf, 1869; Tregelles, 1857, etc.), and it is the style found in the Greek textbooks used to teach Greek grammar.]{.class_s1T0}

The Greek minuscules (cursives) which are usually cited are cited only if they differ from the Byzantine text; they are outnumbered three to one by the minuscules which agree with the Byzantine Textus Receptus.

III\. The Lectionaries.

There are about 1,678 of them available for use which contain extracts from the New Testament. They are indicated in the critical apparatus of Nestle's as "lect."

IV\. The Church Fathers.

[There are the "Western Fathers"---Irenaeus (180), Tertullian (150), Cyprian (200), Jerome (345), Augustine (354); the "Alexandrian Fathers"---Clement (200), Origen (184--254, approx.), Didymus (313), Athanasius (297), and Cyril (380); and the "Antiochan Fathers"---Ignatius (35--107), Polycarp (69--155), Lucian (250--312), Diodorus (died 394), Chrysostom (345--407), and Theodoret (397--457). The "Cappadocian Fathers" should be added to these, as connected with the church of Asia Minor and Greece.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2F9}[\[269\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1YH){.class_s1T7 .noteref}

It does not take a genius to see at a glance what is going to happen to the New Testament following its inception. The Church Fathers make up three groups which match the three families of manuscripts suggested by Griesbach in 1796.

No matter how subtle the refinements and "overlaps" and syntheses and conflating and interpolating of future scribes, three things are evident at once to anyone who knows [church history.]{.class_s1T2-0}

[1. The Alexandrian group is going to be a group of dead Orthodox Bible revisers. Athanasius is present to insure Orthodoxy of ]{.class_s1T0}[profession.]{.class_s1T2-1}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a1XY}[\[270\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2G1){.class_s1TN .noteref}[ Clement is present to insure ]{.class_s1T0}[Greek education,]{.class_s1T2-1}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a289}[\[271\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2G2){.class_s1TN .noteref}[ and Origen is present to produce one version ]{.class_s1T0}[per church]{.class_s1T2-1}[. Any system of determining the "purity," "value," or "quality" of manuscripts from Alexandria, Egypt, that doesn't take the above into account is an impotent system.]{.class_s1T0}

The Alexandrian group is going to approach the Bible exactly as the revision committees of 1901 and 1884 approached it; and any man in the group could be transported bodily into the Episcopal or Presbyterian church of 1970 and adjust himself to the "worship service" in five minutes.

[2. The Roman group (Western Fathers) is going to be a group of Catholics who worship traditions and look to an authoritative hierarchy instead of an authoritative Bible. Irenaeus (130--202) is there with his baby sprinkling]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a23D}[\[272\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2BT){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ to insure that members of the family won't leave the church. Cyprian (200--258) is present to make the bishop into a god,]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2K9}[\[273\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2BU){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ and Augustine (354--430) is there to teach that the sacraments are the "means of Salvation."]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2DT}[\[274\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2BV){.class_s1T7 .noteref}

[The Western group is going to approach the Bible exactly as the College of Cardinals approaches it today; and any man in the group (with the exception of Tertullian \[160--220\])]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a1U1}[\[275\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2KH){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ could walk into St. Peter's and get a "blessing" from the service.]{.class_s1T0}

[3. The Syrian group (Antiochan Fathers) is plainly a group of Bible-believing, Bible-preaching people who were first called "Christians" at Antioch]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a1U4}[\[276\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2FW){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ and were the first to send out missionaries with the gospel (Acts 13:1--5). Any "neutral approach" which refuses to give precedence to THIS type of text (in order to appear scholarly) must ignore ]{.class_s1T0}[the facts of church history ]{.class_s1T2-1}[while searching for the "original manuscripts."]{.class_s1T0}

[Thus, to be really "neutral" one must ]{.class_s1T0}[reject evidence]{.class_s1T2-1}[. Church history turns out to be a demonstration of the effectiveness of the Syrian type text, connected with Antioch and Asia Minor, and the []{#cF7.xhtml_page_77}ineffectiveness of the Alexandrian type text, connected with Italy and North Africa. Only by isolating the Bible from history can one arrive at the conclusions arrived at by Westcott and Hort. They evidently knew nothing about the history of the Christian church, or if they did, they rejected it as having any connection with the manuscripts which professed to be the "treasure" of the true Christian.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2GB}[\[277\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1UC){.class_s1T7 .noteref}

An [ASV ]{.class_s1T2-0}(1901) would match the Alexandrian Fathers; an [RSV ]{.class_s1T2-0}with the Apocrypha would match the Western Fathers; and an [AV ]{.class_s1T2-0}1611 would go with the Antiochan Fathers like gravy goes with rice.

V. The Early Translations.

The first of these would be the Syrian and Latin translations.

[The history of these translations parallels that of the Greek text. There were scores of Latin and Syriac New Testaments circulating all over Asia Minor, Africa, and Palestine, and these Bibles were revised by Jerome (382--470) and Bishop Rabulla (411--435).]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a1TC}[\[278\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2K6){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ Where Rabulla and Jerome followed the corrupt Hesychian (Alexandrian) scholarship of Origen, nearly two centuries before, they mutilated the New Testament text.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2FV}[\[279\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2K7){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ Errors in the ]{.class_s1T0}[Peshitta ]{.class_s1T2-1}[and the ]{.class_s1T0}[Vulgate ]{.class_s1T2-1}[can be traced to the Vatican manuscript and its ancestors.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a27X}[\[280\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2K8){.class_s1T7 .noteref}

[The Old Latin manuscripts date from the second century,]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2K2}[\[281\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2D7){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ and those used by the Waldensians (1170--1600) do not contain the Apocrypha.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a23G}[\[282\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2D8){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ The Apocrypha was added to many Old Latin manuscripts by admirers of Origen and Augustine.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a24S}[\[283\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2D9){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ Tertullian speaks of a complete Latin Bible which was circulating all over North Africa as far back as 190, and this Bible was from manuscripts far superior to anything Rome had in A.D. 350.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a23U}[\[284\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2DA){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ This "Old Latin" was constantly being brought back into European Bibles and used instead of Jerome, and Cassiodorus (540) had it revised to bring it in line with the corrupt "LXX" of Origen.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2FF}[\[285\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2DB){.class_s1T7 .noteref}

[As the "original Greek Bible" is judged by Origen's Hexapla in Vaticanus, so the "majority of scholars" judge the first Latin Bible by Jerome's ]{.class_s1T0}[Vulgate ]{.class_s1T2-1}[where it went by Vaticanus.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a24M}[\[286\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a241){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ Thus, Origen has a hand in corrupting all three Bibles---the Old Testament Hebrew, the New Testament Greek, and the Latin Vulgate.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2JH}[\[287\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a242){.class_s1T7 .noteref}

[The first Latin version was circulating before A.D. 210 and it (as []{#cF7.xhtml_page_78}the Byzantine Greek Receptus) was the work of the spontaneous efforts of African Christians.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2E3}[\[288\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2FA){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ Jerome's version is an official revision of this text, exactly as the ]{.class_s1T0}[ASV ]{.class_s1T2-1}[and ]{.class_s1T0}[RSV ]{.class_s1T2-1}[are official revisions of the Received Greek text. The real "Bible" was copied by hand from A.D. 100--400 by common ordinary Christians who recognize at sight the corrupt Bibles when they saw one. The Albigenses continued to use this "Old Latin" long after Jerome's Vulgate came out,]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2A7}[\[289\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2FB){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ and their preservation of this text is attributed (according to Burkitt) to the fact that they were "heretics"!]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2K1}[\[290\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2FC){.class_s1T7 .noteref}

There are thirty-eight codices which comprise the Latin manuscripts for these Latin versions. A great deal of argument has arisen over the European and African types found among them; and there has been considerable discussion as to whether or not the "Itala," the Old Latin, and the [Vulgate ]{.class_s1T2-0}are the same families.

[Jerome's attitude toward the Old Latin is quite clear.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2HC}[\[291\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1TF){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ He brags about exclusive "vellum scrolls" which the "scholars" have that are "far superior to the Bibles used by the common people," etc., and carries on like any professor in Union Theological Seminary.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a21A}[\[292\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1TG){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ Augustine agrees with Jerome that the common people don't know what they are doing and need a little help with the "archaic words," etc.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a29B}[\[293\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1TH){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ In his letters, Jerome (as the "majority of scholars") refers not only to the "original Greek" but also to the ]{.class_s1T0}["Greek original," ]{.class_s1T2-1}[and he tells us that he will use this "Greek original" to correct the unskillful scribes!]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a29V}[\[294\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1TJ){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ What Greek "original" did he have outside of Origen's Hexapla?]{.class_s1T0}

[The Latin versions are referred to on page 71 of Nestle's introductory notes, and the manuscripts are enumerated by the small, slanting, lower case letters a,b,c,d,e,k, etc. They bear witness to the Syrian type text of the Receptus (where the scholars of Alexandria have not "messed" with them), and they bear witness to Origen's Hexapla (commonly miscalled "The Septuagint"), where Alexandrian scribes got their hands on them. Both Augustine (354--430) and Tertullian (160--220) testify that the scribes in Africa couldn't keep their hands off Bible manuscripts and everybody there messed with them constantly.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2ED}[\[295\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a292){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ This explains satisfactorily the confused condition of the "Itala" and the "Old Latin" by the time of []{#cF7.xhtml_page_79}Jerome. It also indicates who the real "revisers" and "conflaters" of the originals were---they were certainly not the disciples called "Christians" at Antioch (Acts 11:26).]{.class_s1T0}

The Syrian versions are far more interesting than the Latin versions for two reasons.

[1. The majority of autographs of the original New Testament writers were in Asia Minor and Syria.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2E8}[\[296\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a23X){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ (To this, all agree.)]{.class_s1T0}

[2. Since this was in the closest proximity to Syria, the early Syrian manuscripts may have been copied from the originals themselves.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2KJ}[\[297\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a26R){.class_s1T7 .noteref}

[The standard approach toward this text is to judge the early Syrian manuscripts by the ]{.class_s1T0}[Peshitta]{.class_s1T2-1}[.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a1X5}[\[298\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1ZF){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ The word "Peshitta" means "simple" (easy to be understood).]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2A4}[\[299\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1ZG){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ In its original form, it contained the Old Testament as it stands in the ]{.class_s1T0}[AV ]{.class_s1T2-1}[1611 and the New Testament as it stands in the ]{.class_s1T0}[AV ]{.class_s1T2-1}[1611.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a29D}[\[300\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1ZH){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ Corruption's did not enter the text until the middle of the third century, at the time when Origen moved from Alexandria to Caesarea (bringing his publishing company with him).]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a218}[\[301\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1ZJ){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ From then on, and especially during the time of Eusebius and Pamphilus (260--340), the ]{.class_s1T0}[Peshitta ]{.class_s1T2-1}[disintegrated into its present condition and into the types known today as the Philoxenian (485--519), the Harclean (616), and the Jerusalem Syriac (a lectionary of the Gospels, date unknown).]{.class_s1T0}

[The keenest analysis of the ]{.class_s1T0}[Peshitta ]{.class_s1T2-1}[problem and its relation to the Byzantine Receptus has been given by Dr. Edward Hills in his notable work on that subject.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2MZ}[\[302\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a20E){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ Dr. Hills adroitly disassembles the Westcott and Hort theory on the Peshitta and proves conclusively (using the works of Burkitt, Mingana, Voobus, M. Black, and A. C. Clark) that the Syrian text which bears witness to the ]{.class_s1T0}[AV ]{.class_s1T2-1}[readings is older by 100 years than either Vaticanus or Sinaiticus.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a27S}[\[303\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a20F){.class_s1T7 .noteref}

"Tatian's Diatessaron," by Tatian of Assyria (110--172), still survives in the publications of Zahn (1881), Ciasca (1888), and Mosinger's introduction (Ephraem's Com. Venet. 1876). Theodoret (390--458) found more than 200 copies of it circulating in Asia Minor, and they were there before A.D. 160.[]{#cF7.xhtml_a1TD .class-0}[\[304\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1YT){.class_s1T7 .noteref} Readers will be surprised to find that Tatian reads with the [King James Bible ]{.class_s1T2-0}on Luke []{#cF7.xhtml_page_80}2:33 and John 9:35, upholding the Deity of Christ and the Virgin Birth. This gives a definite Syrian witness to the [AV ]{.class_s1T2-0}readings [200 years older than Vaticanus or Sinaiticus]{.class_s1T2-0}.

[The "Curetonian Syriac" consists of fragments of the gospels brought in 1842 from the Nitrain Desert in Egypt that are now in the British Museum. The fragments are from the second to the fifth century A.D.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a22Y}[\[305\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1TV){.class_s1T7 .noteref}

[The Sinaitic Syriac was found in 1892 as a text of the four Gospels. It was found in the monastery of St. Catherine, where Tischendorf found the Sinaiticus manuscript.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2JM}[\[306\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a22X){.class_s1T7 .noteref}

[Syriac translations are indicated in Nestle's apparatus by "sy," followed by other designations which indicate whether they are Curetonian, Philoxenian, Sinaitic, Jerusalem, Harclean, or Peshitta.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a26P}[\[307\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a21T){.class_s1T7 .noteref}

[Besides the early Latin and Syrian translations are the Egyptian translations---the Sahidic and Bohairic. These are called "Coptic" translations and represent the Southern translation---Sahidic, and the Northern---Bohairic. The Sahidic has about five manuscripts for purposes of reconstruction and the Bohairic has about eighty manuscripts.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a21P}[\[308\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1ZY){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ Being closer to Alexandria than the Syrian translations (or even the Latin, as some Latin becomes European), the Coptic usually agrees with Origen's corrupt "LXX."]{.class_s1T0}

[Other than the Coptic versions, the Latin versions, and the Syriac versions, the most important one was the one produced by the "little word" (Ulfilas), a missionary bishop to the Goths.]{.class_s206}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2AS}[\[309\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a28R){.class_s284 .noteref}[ This Bible was in circulation before Vaticanus was written (A.D. 350), and according to Kenyon, the text in it is for the most part that which is found in the Textus Receptus of the ]{.class_s206}[AV ]{.class_s207-1}[1611.]{.class_s206}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a297}[\[310\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a28S){.class_s284 .noteref}

[The Coptic translations from the third to the sixth ]{.class_s1T0}\
[century (in addition to the Sahidic and Bohairic) are the Fayyumic, the Achmimic, and the Sub-Achmimic.]{.class_s1T0}

In addition to these basic ancient versions, one might include three Ethiopic versions from the sixth century, the Georgian version from the fifth century, the Nubian from the sixth century, and the Arabic, Old High German, Persian, Provencial (old French), and Old Slavonic.

[Any study of the ancient versions will reveal a pattern that is unmistakable. The Latin, Syriac, Coptic, and Gothic versions were originally true and trustworthy copies of the original New Testament documents. Then in "the tunneling period"(i.e., during the Roman persecutions), someone (or some group of people) convinced certain Christians that these translations were "archaic," "corrupt," and not based on the "best manuscript evidence." Whoever proposed these suggestions was kin to the gentleman of Genesis 3:1. The only basis for "correcting" could have been a pre-Christian text, and the only ]{.class_s1T0}[pre-Christian ]{.class_s1T2-1}[text was ]{.class_s1T0}[the Old Testament]{.class_s1T2-1}[, and the only Latin, Syrian, Coptic, and Gothic Old Testaments available were ]{.class_s1T0}[available in Hebrew, unless . . . ! ]{.class_s1T2-1}[Unless some scholar who represented a great "cultural center of scientific exegesis" professed to have a ]{.class_s1T0}[Greek Old Testament superior to the Hebrew!]{.class_s1T2-1}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2KR}[\[311\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1TP){.class_s1TN .noteref}[ Since no such Greek Testament appears anywhere before A.D. 120, it is absolutely certain that the corruption's found in the ancient translations are due to incorporation's from Origen's Hexapla or the Apocrypha, written between 200 B.C. and the time of Christ.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2MT}[\[312\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1TR){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ Since the fifth column of Origen's Hexapla is substantially Vaticanus, ]{.class_s1T0}[which includes the Apocrypha]{.class_s1T2-1}[, there is no longer any doubt about errors in the ancient versions.]{.class_s1T0}

The identical phenomenon can be seen today. A Martian from outer space, rummaging around through the ruins of a bombed out earth, would find [AV ]{.class_s1T2-0}1611 Bibles, [RV ]{.class_s1T2-0}Bibles, [ASV ]{.class_s1T2-0}Bibles, [RSV ]{.class_s1T2-0}Bibles, [Amplified Bibles]{.class_s1T2-0}, Moffatt, Weymouth, Goodspeed, etc., and in attempting a reconstruction of text, he would assume that the [AV ]{.class_s1T2-0}1611 was a "conflation" of the other Bibles.[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2FK .class-0}[\[313\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a24K){.class_s1T7 .noteref}

The fact that the [Amplified Version ]{.class_s1T2-0}was obviously a "conflation" of the [AV]{.class_s1T2-0}, [ASV]{.class_s1T2-0}, and [RSV ]{.class_s1T2-0}would not bother him in the least! (It didn't bother Wescott and Hort in the least!) The "man from Mars" would assume that a brand-new copy of the [RV ]{.class_s1T2-0}(which was left on a library shelf from 1881--1990) was a "pure and neutral text." He would then assume that the worn and torn [AV ]{.class_s1T2-0}1611 of Billy Sunday (with notes scribbled all over it) was a "scribal corruption" of the original with a "doctrinal bias" that made it "untrustworthy."[]{#cF7.xhtml_a23Y .class-0}[\[314\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2C6){.class_s1T7 .noteref} Going by the dictum that the "shorter reading" is the best one, the Martian would assume that the [RSV ]{.class_s1T2-0}text was the original, although, in actuality, []{#cF7.xhtml_page_82 .class-0}[it was 340 years later than the AV 1611! ]{.class_s1T2-0}What the Martian would do with the Apocrypha in the Catholic [RSV ]{.class_s1T2-0}is something else, for if the "shorter reading" is the best one, then Vaticanus and Sinaiticus should both be scratched at the start of the investigation; they both contain half a dozen books that have been [added ]{.class_s1T2-0}to the Scriptures.

Is it not more reasonable to suppose that the [AV ]{.class_s1T2-0}1611 represents a purified text which has at last "cleaned up" from the corruption of thirteen centuries? At least England is an "island," which might fit into Westcott and Hort's remarkable statement that the purest manuscripts were preserved "on the island of neutrality."

[In all the ancient versions we see corrupting influence operating between A.D. 150 and A.D. 400. What survives this period is two sets of manuscripts.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a1WG}[\[315\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1X7){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ One of these contains the Book of Revelation, omits the Apocrypha (as part of the Old testament), and upholds the Deity of Jesus Christ.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2BZ}[\[316\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1X8){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ The other set often omits the Book of Revelation, includes the Apocrypha as part of the Old Testament, and attacks the Deity of Jesus Christ. (See Acts 20:28; John 1:18; Luke 2:33; 1 Tim. 3:16; Mark 1:1; Luke 23:42; Matt. 24:36; Rom. 14:10; Col. 2:9--10;  John 3:13; and John 9:35.) Variations in the fifth-century Peshitta (from the Greek Receptus of the ]{.class_s1T0}[AV ]{.class_s1T2-1}[1611) can easily be accounted for in this fashion.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a25C}[\[317\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1X9){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ As a matter of fact, the corrupting influence of Origen and the mythological LXX can be seen down through the centuries surviving occasionally even in the Byzantine readings.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2N5}[\[318\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1XA){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ Were it not for the providential preservation of the word by the Holy Spirit of God, Greek scholars would have destroyed the Christian's New Testament seventeen centuries ago!]{.class_s1T0}

VI\. The Papyrus Fragments.

[The papyrus is obviously the source for our word "paper." Herodotus (484--425) B.C.) calls the papyrus "parchment."]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a23H}[\[319\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2MB){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ It was made from the byblos plant and constituted a cheap paper similar to modern day "newsprint." It was the "poor man's" writing material and before it was used in codex form (like a modern book), it was used as a roll, written on both sides.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2H2}[\[320\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2MC){.class_s1T7 .noteref}

[It is highly probable that the codex was invented by soul-winning personal workers who carried New Testaments with them.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a1VH}[\[321\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a28C){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ It is certain that no real second-century Christian would have been caught dead with "vellum scrolls" on him or the high-class "revised versions" put out by Alexandria. Rather, the first and second century Bible-believing people used papyrus rolls and codices which they copied by hand from one another.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2KP}[\[322\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a28D){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ This explains why few papyrus copies of the Receptus survived the first three centuries of Roman persecution. The majority of papyrus fragments which survived were fragments like P66 and P75, which Christians refused to copy because they recognized Origen's handwriting when they saw it.]{.class_s1T0}

[However, as any other set of manuscripts, many readings in the papyrus from the second and third centuries agree with the readings of the ]{.class_s1T0}[AV ]{.class_s1T2-1}[1611 (much to the consternation of Westcott and Hort, who insisted that the readings of the ]{.class_s1T0}[AV ]{.class_s1T2-1}[1611 had to be]{.class_s1T0}[ late readings).]{.class_s1T2-1}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2G3}[\[323\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a27W){.class_s1TN .noteref}

[The papyri were numbered 1 through 19 at the time of Kenyon's list, published in 1912 (]{.class_s1T0}[The Handbook of the Textual Criticism of the New Testament]{.class_s1T2-1}[).]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2CB}[\[324\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a20A){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ Most of them were found at Oxyrhynchus, 120 miles south of Cairo in the Libyan Desert. The average roll was 30 inches long and 9 to 10 inches wide.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a1Z7}[\[325\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a20B){.class_s1T7 .noteref}

P1 has portions of Matthew chapter 1 from the third century.

P2 has portions of John chapters 12 and Luke, chapter 7 in Sahidic and Greek from the fifth and sixth centuries.

P3 has parts of Luke chapters 7 and 10 from the sixth century.

P4 has parts of Luke chapters 1, 5, and 6 from the fourth century. It was found joined to a manuscript [written by Philo!]{.class_s1T2-0}

P5 has parts of John chapters 1 and 20 from the third century.

P6 has John 11:45

P7 has Luke 4:1--2

P8 has portions of Acts chapters 4--6 from the fourth century.

P9 has portions of 1 John chapter 4 from the fourth and fifth century.

P10 has part of Romans chapter 1 from the fourth century.

P11 has parts of 1 Corinthians chapters 1,6, and 7 from the fifth century.

P12 has Hebrews 1:1 from the third or fourth century.

P13 has parts of Hebrews chapters 2, 5, 10, 11, and 12 from the fourth century.

P14 has portions of 1 Corinthians chapters 1--3 from the fifth century.

P15 has parts of 1 Corinthians chapter 7, Philippians chapters 3 and 4 from the fourth century.

P16 has Romans 12:3--8 from the sixth and seventh centuries.

P17 has Titus 1:11--15 and 2:3--8 from the third century.

P18 has Hebrews 9:12--19 from the fourth century.

P19 has Revelation 1:4--7 from the third century.

[(An interesting thing about these papyri is that they indicate that the Alexandrian scholars perverted the original Receptus from the papyri in order to manufacture the Vatican text.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a221}[\[326\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2DD){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ This is proved by Porter's study on the readings of Papyrus 75, which was carried further by Edward Hills \[1967\] in his work on ]{.class_s1T0}[Believing Bible Study.]{.class_s1T2-1}[ Comparisons of P66, Aleph \[Sinaiticus\], P75, and "D" \[representing the Western family of manuscripts\] show that the Alexandrian scribes took papyrus Bibles \[used by common, ordinary Christians\] and manufactured the "official Alexandrian" text which survives today in the ]{.class_s1T0}[ASV ]{.class_s1T2-1}[\[1901\] and the ]{.class_s1T0}[RSV ]{.class_s1T2-1}[\[1952\].)]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2H4}[\[327\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2DE){.class_s1T7 .noteref}

In addition to this collection, we have the Chester Beatty fragments, published in 1933--37, and the Bodmer papyri, published in 1956--62. With the Bodmer papyri, the Beatty papyri, and the Rylands papyri, a considerable number of Biblical fragments have been assembled. They are listed in the critical apparatus of Nestle's with the letter "P" followed by a small raised number.

[There are about 54 papyrus fragments now available and they are numbered from 1 up to 75. Only 23 were published by 1939, but since then the number has increased.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a1UH}[\[328\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a29F){.class_s1T7 .noteref}

[A complete list of the Biblical papyri from No. 1 through 76 can be found on pages xi-xiii of the Greek New Testament (1966), published by the "United Bible Societies." Some of them---P74, P68, and P41---run as late as the seventh and eighth centuries A.D. Many of the other papyri which have been discovered are NOT Biblical. They contain everything from Homer to grocery lists, and the Bible believer must not be deceived into thinking that just because []{#cF7.xhtml_page_85}someone hollers, "papyrus!" that this means he is going to get "the original Greek."]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2B9}[\[329\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2C2){.class_s1T7 .noteref}

The student will observe, further, that very often in the critical apparatus of Nestle's New Testament the testimony of early papyri is rejected [because it agrees with the AV 1611 readings. ]{.class_s1T2-0}This will be gone into in detail in the next chapter, but the young minister who has been brainwashed into thinking that the [ASV ]{.class_s1T2-0}and [RSV ]{.class_s1T2-0}texts always use "the best manuscripts" or "the oldest manuscripts" should observe that where the "oldest manuscripts" [reinforce the AV 1611 text, they are often rejected. ]{.class_s1T2-0}(See, for example, Matt. 22:30, 27:46, 27:49--50; Rev. 11:11, 12:5; Rom. 13:9, etc.) Even with these few examples, the alert and attentive student can see that the "scientific text" created by Nestle and Westcott and Hort and others is filled with inconsistencies and arbitrary judgments which are based on [an irrational prejudice ]{.class_s1T2-0}against one family of manuscripts---the Syrian (or Byzantine) type.[]{#cF7.xhtml_a26E .class-0}[\[330\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1T8){.class_s1T7 .noteref}

Neither Westcott and Hort, Weiss, nor Nestle will retain their favorite manuscripts every time where they support the [AV ]{.class_s1T2-0}1611. There are scores of places where even "Vaticanus" is junked because it agrees with the Textus Receptus of Antioch and Syria.[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2A3 .class-0}[\[331\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1WD){.class_s1T7 .noteref} It would seem, from a thorough study of the critical apparatus in most Greek editions, that the purpose of the editor is to place [as many AV 1611 readings in the margin or footnotes as possible, and any stratagem ]{.class_s1T2-0}is legal in order to accomplish this. The real scholar will not accept such nonsense as "modern scholars" accept and put out [without checking it carefully]{.class_s1T2-0}. The briefest "check" will reveal papyri, Aleph, "B," and "A" (Alexandrinus) pitched into the footnotes time and time again where they support the readings of the 1611 Authorized Holy Bible.

The most interesting thing about the papyri is the fact that several of them have texts on Revelation---P47 for example. This brings up a very interesting question. How is it that "Vaticanus" (written in A.D. 350) doesn't have the book of Revelation in it, while the [AV ]{.class_s1T2-0}1611 (written 1230 years later) [does?]{.class_s1T2-0}

Can one explain how Erasmus' "late manuscripts" contained [a whole book ]{.class_s1T2-0}missing in the "pure, neutral, Vatican text."!

How does one explain the [AV ]{.class_s1T2-0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_page_86 .class-0}1611 containing the text of a third-century Greek papyrus manuscript, while the [fourth century Vaticanus is lacking it? ]{.class_s1T2-0}Didn't the writer of Vaticanus have access to the book? Didn't he have access to P47?

How did Erasmus know the book of Revelation should be in the canon when the "best manuscript" (according to Westcott and Hort [doesn't even have it?]{.class_s1T2-0}

(A man conjectures) "Well, it was [lost."]{.class_s1T2-0} But isn't this a little farfetched? How could it have [gotten lost ]{.class_s1T2-0}when it was written on [a thick, tanned, animal hide ]{.class_s1T2-0}which to this day is called "the best preserved text" available? P46, written even earlier, has survived with a complete text of 1 Corinthians! How is it that the carefully guarded and well-preserved text, written on imperishable material, could not preserve the book which speaks of, ["Mystery, Babylon the Great . . . The seven heads are seven mountains, on which the woman sitteth . . . And the woman is that great city, which reigneth over the kings of the earth"]{.class_s1T1-0} (Rev. 17). Convenient omission, eh what?

Isn't that the most expedient thing you ever saw for a Vatican manuscript kept in the Vatican?

VII\. The Conjectures of Scholars.

Those referred to most often are either the Church Fathers or the editors of the critical editions themselves; these would include Alford (1810--1871), Weiss (1913), Von Soden (1852--1914), Origen (184--254), Irenaeus (130--202), Westcott and Hort (1884), etc. A "conjecture" is a "guess." It is called a "theory" or "hypothesis" in scientific circles to give it prestige, but it is still a guess.

VIII\. The Sermons of Early Preachers.

These are valuable as they usually contain dozens of quotations from the New Testament. The "Church Fathers" (listed under IV) are the ones whose sermons are usually referred to when an effort is being made to establish a text. This is not entirely satisfactory as it leads the investigator into the booby trap of what might be called "The Pauline Obsession." This is a peculiar obsession which affects [writers]{.class_s1T2-0}. Briefly, it may be stated as that feeling that the "great men" of Christian history are the [writers ]{.class_s1T2-0}or men who left [written works]{.class_s1T2-0}. The psychology behind this is the fact that [men wrote the Bible; ]{.class_s1T2-0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_page_87 .class-0}therefore, a certain prestige surrounds that branch of Christendom which [writes]{.class_s1T2-0}. But this is a false lead. Anyone familiar with church history is aware of the thousands upon thousands of Christian men and women who lived, loved God, stood by his Word, and suffered and died for it [without putting anything on paper]{.class_s1T2-0}.[]{#cF7.xhtml_a1XG .class-0}[\[332\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a23V){.class_s1T7 .noteref} To judge true Christianity (or the text of a true Bible) by the writings of men whose [motives for writing may be mixed is an error]{.class_s1T2-0}. This is why Martin Luther referred to the "Church Fathers" as the "Church babies" and thundered,[ "What saith the Scriptures?!"]{.class_s1T1-0}

[The Pauline obsession is most manifest in the way by which writers after Paul's time like to classify dead Orthodox theologians and apologists with him.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a1UK}[\[333\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1X0){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ It is assumed because Paul ]{.class_s1T0}[wrote ]{.class_s1T2-1}[and ]{.class_s1T0}[defended ]{.class_s1T2-1}[the Christian faith that this puts him in brackets with Calvin, Augustine, Cyprian, Origen, Aquinas, Irenaeus, Jerome, Westcott and Hort, and Berkhof; but this assumption is a lying presumption. Paul was a ]{.class_s1T0}[street preacher ]{.class_s1T2-1}[who was thrown in jail for preaching 1 Corinthians 15:1--4. He did not hammer out his apologetics in an air-conditioned office with a coke machine down the hallway, and he would quote from heathen poets]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a1WT}[\[334\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1X1){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ before he would mention Eccleasticus, Bel and the Dragon, the Wisdom of Ben Sirach, Tobit, or Judith.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a1WC}[\[335\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1X2){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ Scholars and church historians are highly mistaken when they swallow ]{.class_s1T0}[the writings ]{.class_s1T2-1}[of Cyprian (200--258), Clement (30--100), Irenaeus (130--202), Augustine (354--430), and Origen (184--254) as true representatives of Biblical Christianity.]{.class_s1T0}

The [sermons]{.class_s1T1-0}, therefore, of the early preachers may help somewhat to establish an early text, but if that text does not [turn out to be the text ]{.class_s1T2-0}of John Huss (1369--1415), Martin Luther (1483--1546), Tyndale (1494--1536), the Waldensians, the Huguenots, the Albigenses, and the martyrs and missionaries of the ages, it is [a counterfeit ]{.class_s1T2-0}which God will not honor.

[Now, all of the materials discussed beforehand have been lumped into "families." This idea came from Griesbach (1796), who was seeking to elevate his own critical edition to the preeminent place.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2EA}[\[336\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a26S){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ The "Emphatic Diaglot" which he published (1774, 1796, 1806) gave the Pope's manuscript the first place. From this time on, []{#cF7.xhtml_page_88}the Vatican manuscript was given all the publicity it needed (much like the inferior painting of da Vinci!), and Griesbach was hailed as the "saviour from corrupt Bibles," ]{.class_s1T0}[such as the Bibles of the Reformation!]{.class_s1T2-1}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a20S}[\[337\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a26T){.class_s1TN .noteref}

[In order to magnify the Vatican manuscript and make it appear to be more authentic than the Receptus, Griesbach hit upon the novel idea of dividing the manuscripts into three families---Western, Syrian, and Alexandrian.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a1YM}[\[338\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2J8){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ Having done this, he assigned ]{.class_s1T0}[all the early manuscripts to the Alexandrian family (!) ]{.class_s1T2-1}[leaving the Syrian text standing like a cold cat in the snow with nothing but ]{.class_s1T0}[late manuscripts to support it. ]{.class_s1T2-1}[Thus, the gullible twentieth-century student is faced with the formidable array of "Aleph," A, B, and C, as opposed to the ]{.class_s1T0}[AV ]{.class_s1T2-1}[1611, and even "D" (Western) in the lineup against it!]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2BY}[\[339\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2J9){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ A formidable amount of "evidence" if you ever saw it! Who could hold out with E, F, G, and H, against ]{.class_s1T0}[A, B, C, and D!?]{.class_s1T2-1}

From the day that Griesbach invented this arbitrary classification to this day, the "majority of scholars" think that A, B, C, etc., are [one family ]{.class_s1T2-0}and that E, F, G, etc., are [another]{.class_s1T2-0}. Has anyone noticed that Aleph, B, A, and C [are 90 percent  the text of the AV 1611? ]{.class_s1T2-0}What made them different from the Receptus Greek manuscripts was not a "family difference." The difference was that the Receptus manuscripts exalted Jesus Christ in about ten passages and the "Alexandrian family" of manuscripts low rated Him! The total doctrinal corruption's are about 152 out of 8000 verses, otherwise the [ASV ]{.class_s1T2-0}and the [RSV ]{.class_s1T2-0}have copied the [AV ]{.class_s1T2-0}1611 90 percent of the time.

[The criteria for the "family" setup is "The type of text which built up in a certain area." This may be true, but it cannot alter the fact that one true text could have existed from A.D. 50 to A.D. 1519 with different localities altering certain verses in line with Origen's corrupt Hexapla. This may be seen immediately when one examines "A" (Alexandrinus). Whereas, it has been classified as an "Alexandrian type" manuscript (Hesychian or Egyptian), it plainly bears witness to the Reformation Bibles over and over again.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2HE}[\[340\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a23E){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ The same is true of "C" (Ephraemi Rescriptus), and the same is true of "Aleph" (Sinaiticus).]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a1XP}[\[341\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a23F){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ (These statements will be proven beyond []{#cF7.xhtml_page_89}any shadow of a doubt in the next chapter.)]{.class_s1T0}

The families of manuscripts are said to be constructed on the basis of:

1. "Are a manuscript's readings characteristic of that family?"

2. "Do manuscripts from that area (Western, Alexandrian, Syrian) contain the same readings?"

Without going into a long thing here, let the Bible-believing Christian observe that the [characteristic readings ]{.class_s1T2-0}of the Alexandrian family are that they "Characteristically" [low rate the Lord Jesus Christ.]{.class_s1T2-0}

From the "family" idea, Westcott and Hort (1884) agreed with Griesbach (1796) that "B" (Vaticanus) was a "remarkably pure text" written somewhere in the West. (Some scholars today have abandoned that theory---as we remarked before---but all the Greek faculty members of the Conservative schools still believe it as much as Catholics believe that birth control will cut down church membership).

[By diverting everyone's attention to the "families," Griesbach and Westcott and Hort were able to focus attention on the corrupt fifth column of Origen's Hexapla.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a2N3}[\[342\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2DW){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ When this was done, the arguments in the seminaries (Liberal and Conservative alike) no longer revolved around the Syrian text at all, but were continually revolving around Western or Alexandrian authority. Clark (1926) said that the Western type was first and the Alexandrian scholars copied it, omitting some of the Western readings.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a20T}[\[343\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2DX){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ Ropes (1926) said that the Alexandrian type was first and that the Western copied it and ]{.class_s1T0}[added ]{.class_s1T2-1}[to it.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a1YS}[\[344\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2DY){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ Here the scholars seem to have run out of ideas.]{.class_s1T0}

[There is a third theory, propounded in 1881 by Dean Burgon of Chichester (1813--1888), which evidently no one remembers.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cF7.xhtml_a214}[\[345\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2JA){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ This theory, which matches ]{.class_s1T0}[all the facts of history, all the evidence of the papyri, all the evidence found in the uncials, all the evidences of soul winning and revival, and all the evidences of common sense and reason, is that the SYRIAN TEXT was FIRST and the Alexandrian scribes SUBTRACTED FROM IT (ASV, RSV) and the Roman scribes ADDED TO IT (Vulgate, Douay-Rheims). ]{.class_s1T2-1}[]{#cF7.xhtml_page_90}[This theory, supported by Scrivener, Burgon, Miller, and Hills, tallies perfectly with ]{.class_s1T0}[everything]{.class_s1T2-1}[.]{.class_s1T0}

While Rome and Alexandria were arguing about textual criticism and manuscript evidence, God was using His Holy Bible all over Africa and Asia, [and is still doing it]{.class_s1T2-0}.[]{#cF7.xhtml_a1TU .class-0}[\[346\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2KT){.class_s1T7 .noteref} Why would any "authoritative" text come from [Rome or Alexandria? ]{.class_s1T2-0}What does the Bible [say ]{.class_s1T2-0}about Rome and Egypt? Is this the proper place to bring the matter up? If not, since when did a [Christian ]{.class_s1T2-0}scholar abandon [what the Bible SAID about Egypt and Rome when examining the "Bibles" that came from these places?]{.class_s1T2-0}

Is not the Bible more authoritative [than any of the men who revised it?]{.class_s1T2-0}

Having briefly listed the materials with which the researcher can construct a Greek text, let us now turn our attention to how these materials were used (and misused) in constructing the new Roman Catholic Bible, commonly miscalled "the Westcott and Hort Greek text."

[]{#cNE.xhtml}

# [Chapter 7 - ]{.class_s1WA}[]{#cNE.xhtml_page_91}[The Great Juggling Act]{.class_s1WB} {.heading_s3E-0}

Having listed the materials with which the critics work as they seek to destroy the Reformation Bibles, we now turn to the manner in which these materials have been employed since 1881.

First, we shall examine those places where the "modern scholars" go back on their word and reject the evidence of their own manuscripts where they agree with the Receptus or the [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611. Secondly, we shall examine the pro-Catholic readings of the [ASV ]{.class_s1SV-0}and [RSV ]{.class_s1SV-0}where they return to Jerome's Vulgate (340--420), via the corrupt Greek manuscripts of Alexandria. Thirdly, we shall examine those places in the Catholic Bible which are truer to the word of God than the "new" Bibles. Fourthly, we shall examine the disputed passages in the [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611---I John 5:7; John 5:3--4, 7:53--8:11; and Mark 16:9--20.

I. Places where Westcott and Hort (and Nestle) refuse to abide by their own criteria of judgment.

A. John 14:7. At the close of the verse, the word "αυτον" has been omitted. However, "αυτον" is not only in the Receptus of the [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611, it is found also in P66 (second century, representing the papyrus), Aleph, A (fourth and fifth century, representing the Hesychian texts), D (fifth century, representing the Western texts), Theta (ninth century, representing a family sometimes designated as "Caesarean"), the Vulgate, and the majority of the remaining witnesses. This preponderant evidence is nullified by [two manuscripts (which contain the Apocrypha!)]{.class_s1SV-0}---"B" (fourth century) and "C" (from the fifth century).

One can see at a glance that "B" has been given a value equivalent to [four families of manuscripts]{.class_s1SV-0}, where one manuscript is as old as itself and [one is 100 years OLDER!]{.class_s1SV-0}

[B. John 8:38. Near the end of the verse the reader will see that "εωρακατε" has been deleted and ]{.class_s1SU}\
["ηκουσατε" inserted. The reading (]{.class_s1SU}[AV ]{.class_s1SV-1}[1611) is upheld by P66 (second century), Aleph (fourth century), D (fifth century), the Receptus manuscripts, and the Syriac palimpsest of the fourth century. Nestle gives no documentation for the reading of his text []{#cNE.xhtml_page_92}and leaves us to assume that "B" and "A" have the reading ]{.class_s1SU}\
["ηκουσατε." Since Aleph can cancel "B" in antiquity, and D can cancel "A" in antiquity, we are left with the Receptus manuscripts (which make up the bulk of any set of manuscripts) and a second-century papyrus reading which reads as the ]{.class_s1SU}[AV ]{.class_s1SV-1}[1611. (Those were some "late manuscripts" Erasmus used, weren't they!?)]{.class_s1SU}

C. John 10:40. There is a disagreement over the spelling of ["He remained."]{.class_s2FD} The [King James Bible]{.class_s2A0-0}, with its Receptus (Syrian family) manuscripts, spelled the verb "εμεινεν". Opposing this spelling (in Nestle's) is the spelling "εμενεν." The Vatican manuscript takes Nestle's side against the [AV ]{.class_s2A0-0}1611. By so doing, it must buck P45, P66, P75, Aleph, A, C, D, Theta, and the majority of the remaining witnesses. Here, Nestle (in keeping with his note on p. 68 of the preface) has made the Vatican manuscript (fourth century) superior to Aleph (fourth century), A (fifth century), C (fifth century), D (fifth century), Theta (ninth century), P45 [(third century!)]{.class_s2A0-0}, P66 [(second century!!)]{.class_s2A0-0}, and P57 (third century). That is, when a "modern scholar" tells you that the [AV ]{.class_s2A0-0}readings are from "late manuscripts" and the [ASV ]{.class_s2A0-0}and [RSV ]{.class_s2A0-0}are from "older manuscripts," [he lies.]{.class_s2A0-0}

Here, the [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611 has used Greek manuscripts (unknowingly!) which are 100--200 years earlier than Vaticanus, on which all the "new" Bibles are based.

D. John 12:3. There is another disagreement in spelling. Backing the [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611 is the spelling of the Receptus "Μαρια." Reinforcing this Greek text is P66, Aleph, A, C, D, Theta, the Vulgate, and the majority of manuscripts. Offering "Μαριαμ" instead of "Μαρια" the Vaticanus stands along with a few minuscules. We are to assume that one Vatican reading (in the fourth century) is more authoritative than any other one in the same century supported by earlier readings, plus the majority of manuscripts.

E. Luke 24:6. Here, Westcott and Hort have put in double brackets as a doubtful reading, "ουκ εστιν ωδε αλλα ηγερθη." Nestle calls this a "Western omission," which is "fudging," for all Western readings have it except "D" and one or two Old Latin manuscripts. The [RSV ]{.class_s1SV-0}has consigned the reading to the footnote, and yet, lo and behold, the reading is found in P75 (third century)! How do we account for the fact that the Receptus, used by Martin Luther and the [King James ]{.class_s1SV-0}[]{#cNE.xhtml_page_93 .class-0}translators, had access to a third-century manuscript which Westcott and Hort considered to be "doubtful"! Furthermore, this identical phenomenon is found in Luke 22:19, 24:3, 12, 36, 40, and 52!

1. "το υπερ υμων διδομενον" (Luke 22:19).

2. "του κυριου Ιησου" (Luke 24:3)

3. "Ο δε Πετρος αναστας εδραμεν επι το μνημειον και παρακυψας βλεπει τα οθονια κειμενα, και απηλθεν προς αυτον θαυμαζων το γεγονος" (Luke 24:12).

On this last reading (Luke 24:12), the whole scholastic farce is suddenly manifested where the freshman student can see it. The reading given above is the reading of the [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611. (It is omitted in the [RSV ]{.class_s1SV-0}of 1952; it is also omitted in Nestle's Greek Text.)

But what have we here?!

The reading is supported by Vaticanus! Not only does "B" (Vaticanus) support the [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611 reading, but this time P75, Aleph, A, C, Theta, the Old Latin, and Old Syriac all contain the reading!

What have we here?!

How did this [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611 reading get omitted in a "new" Bible based on "older manuscripts"? What is this "older manuscript" that is more authoritative than A, B, C, Aleph, Theta, and P75? Why bless my soul, it is "D" (Bezae Cantabrigiensis) [from the fifth century.]{.class_s1SV-0}

What could have possessed Nestle and the [RSV ]{.class_s1SV-0}to suddenly reverse field and accept [one Western manuscript ]{.class_s1SV-0}as a higher authority than four Alexandrian manuscripts [which included Vaticanus?!]{.class_s1SV-0}

"Scientific exegesis?"

"Grammatico-historico methods of interpretation?"

"Recent discoveries of [more authentic ]{.class_s1SV-0}manuscripts?"

No. The truth of the matter is the verse had to be deleted to sustain and maintain the theory of Westcott and Hort that the Syrian type text ([AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611) was a "conflation" of Western and Alexandrian readings. The lengths to which these "scholars" will go to bolster this incompetent and ridiculous theory is now demonstrated in Luke 24:12.

If the reading is allowed to remain in the text, it overthrows the whole basis of textual reconstruction used by revision committees []{#cNE.xhtml_page_94}since 1881. For if the Textus Receptus had copied Alexandria, they would have omitted all the Alexandrian omissions that are [also missing ]{.class_s1SV-0}in the Western group; and if they copied the Western group they would have included all the Western readings which Alexandria [omits]{.class_s1SV-0}---Luke 23:48, 3:22, 23:53; Matthew 3:16, 20:28, etc. Isn't it remarkable how the Syrian text knew when to [keep a reading ]{.class_s1SV-0}which was lacking in the Western group, [and when to reject a reading ]{.class_s1SV-0}which was found in the Western group, [and at the same time knew when to retain readings omitted in the Alexandrian group? ]{.class_s1SV-0}In the case before us an additional phenomenon is observed: the Syrian text also knows how to retain an Alexandrian reading when it is correct!

If the Alexandrian family had copied the Western (Clark), where did they get the readings of Luke 22:19, 24:3, 12, 40, and 52? [They got them from the Syrian text WHICH STILL HAS THEM.]{.class_s1SV-0}

If the Western family had copied the Alexandrian (Ropes), where did it get the readings that are missing in the Alexandrian family (Acts 8:37; Luke 9:55--56, etc.)? [They got them from the Syrian text, WHICH STILL HAS THEM.]{.class_s1SV-0}

The man who "deleted" Luke 24:12 from the Holy Bible was Marcion "the Heretic" (120--160). (See Vol. 47, p. 426, 427, of the Corpus Scriptorum Ec­clesiasticorum Latinorum, Academia Litterarum Vindebonesis.) E. Nestle is in [agreement ]{.class_s1SV-0}with Marcion, and he does not fail to let you know that he is---p. 226, [Novum Testamentum Graece]{.class_s1SV-0}, 1898--1963.

Continuing in this list of "Western omissions," we find:

4. "και λεγει αυτοις ειρηνη υμιν" (Luke 24:36).

5. "και τουτο ειπων εδειξεν αυτοις τας χειρας και τους ποδας" (Luke 24:40. Again, we have Marcion "the Heretic" to thank for the omission of these Bible verses from Nestle's New Testament and the [RSV. ]{.class_s1SV-0}P75 has the reading of the [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611, which makes the [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611 at least 200 years older than the [RSV ]{.class_s1SV-0}in its choice of Greek manuscript evidence. P75 is a third-century reading, and the "D" of the [RSV ]{.class_s1SV-0}is a fifth-century reading. Review now the remarks in Chapter Two on the "Revival of Third Century Superstitions"!)

6. "προσκυνησαντες αυτον" (Luke 24:52).

The [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611, plus P75, A, B, C, Theta, Aleph, and the Vulgate, now stands against the [RSV ]{.class_s1SV-0}[]{#cNE.xhtml_page_95 .class-0}(1952), Marcion, "D," and a few old Syriac and Latin readings.

7. "και ανεφερετο εις τον ουρανον" (Luke 24:51).

The [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611, plus P75, A, B, C, Theta, Vulgate, and the vast majority of manuscripts, now reads contrary to the [RSV ]{.class_s1SV-0}(1952), D, Aleph, and [Marcion the Heretic.]{.class_s1SV-0}

A truly nonpartisan, unprejudiced, unbiased, "neutral" critic can see at once that the [RSV]{.class_s1T2-0}, Marcion, and Nestle's Testament have more in common than Capone, Clyde Barrow, Starkweather, and Oswald. They all have a doctrinal prejudice against the Deity of Christ and [the humanity of Christ]{.class_s1T2-0}, and they are no more "neutral" than a Jesuit priest at an inquisition. This is the "scholarship" which is recommended by the faculties of the Fundamental Bible schools in America today! While these faculties would holler bloody murder about an [RSV]{.class_s1T2-0}, they would [without reservation ]{.class_s1T2-0}recommend to their ministerial students the manuscripts from which it came. These manuscripts are the same ones that Dr. Schaff and Dr. Green used [in making the ASV ]{.class_s1T2-0}(1901).

We have only presented "B" in another light here to show you how inconsistent the scholars are in applying their dictums. Here, "B" has been given the footnote seven times in a row to allow "D" (written 200 years later!) to have the limelight as a champion against the inspired words of the Holy Bible.

F. First Corinthians 3:16. Here, the [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611 has used the Receptus manuscript's reading "οικει εν υμιν." This is not the order of the Vatican manuscript, which reads "εν υμιν οικει". The "evidence" for this inversion is "P" (sixth century) and two minuscules!

Reading with the Receptus is P46 (third century), Aleph (fourth century), A (fifth century), D (fifth century), all the Old Latin, and the Receptus uncials from the sixth century to Erasmus. "B" has suddenly [regained ]{.class_s1SV-0}its prestige after playing second fiddle to "D" for eight verses (see above)! Would some enlightened scholar please tell us [how ]{.class_s1SV-0}and [when ]{.class_s1SV-0}"B" suddenly got so valuable again after losing out to manuscripts written 200 years later?

G. First Corinthians 5:4 exhibits the great "juggling act" in full swing. At the beginning of the verse the word "Christ," "Χριστος," []{#cNE.xhtml_page_96}has been omitted by weighing A, B, and D (two fifth century manuscripts and one fourth century manuscript) against P46, Aleph, G, Receptus, and the Old Latin and Old Syriac (one third-century manuscript, one fourth-century manuscript, one tenth-century manuscript, a dozen third--fifth-century versions, and the majority of the uncial manuscripts that remain).

But all of this is only the overture to the show. (Step inside the big top, ladies and gentlemen, and see the "greatest show on earth:"!)

"ημων" has been omitted before "Ιησους." This time, Aleph replaces B as an authority, "A" stays where it is, and "B" jumps over on the side of the Receptus; and once this is done, Nestle cannot tolerate the reading! Therefore, "ημων" has been stuck in the footnote, in spite of the fact that P46 and "B" (Vaticanus) [support it! ]{.class_s1SV-0}(You see, where the Vatican manuscript gets too friendly with the [King James Bible, it is junked!)]{.class_s1SV-0}

H. Mark 6:23. This is exactly what happens again, here. Nestle has dumped "B" in the footnote again (after saying that it should be given "precedence") because it agreed with the Receptus, P45, A, D, and Theta. All of these readings back up the [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611 with "οτι ο εαν με αιτησης." The "με" is omitted in Aleph alone. But "B" got too close to the Receptus so it had to drop out and give Aleph the honors! Is this the "neutral approach"?

I. First Corinthians 13:3. But the best is for the last, and the three-ring circus now enters town; clowns and all. In this text, Westcott and Hort, the [ASV]{.class_s1SV-0}, [RSV]{.class_s1SV-0}, Nestle, and the Vaticanus got into a snarl that they never got out of, and never will. Westcott and Hort, here, accepted the Vatican reading, which Nestle would not dare accept, and this time Nestle abandoned not only Vaticanus, but P46, Sinaiticus (Aleph), and A (Alexandrinus)! Hoping to salvage some of his pride in the wreck of 1 Corinthians 13:3, the redoubtable scholar has grabbed at an incorrect spelling, which no freshman studying Greek grammar would have ever picked up.

The sideshow in the verse is the word "καυθησωμαι," ["in order that I might be burned."]{.class_s1SW-0} This is the reading of the Receptus; however, none of the Hesychian (Alexandrian) manuscripts will back up the reading. According to Westcott and Hort, therefore, this reading should be [rejected]{.class_s1SV-0}. By the dictum of "Vaticanus first" []{#cNE.xhtml_page_97}(Nestle's dictum) it should be rejected. Manuscripts C, D, G, and L back up the word in the Receptus "καυθησωμαι," although they have it in the wrong grammatical case. It is true that "C" has the reading and it is true that Griesbach (in an effort to rob the Receptus of as many manuscripts as possible---see Chapter Six) classified "C" as Hesychian, but a palimpsest (twice-written) manuscript from the fifth century will hardly serve to override "B" (Vaticanus), the darling of the seminaries!

The Hesychian texts (Aleph, A, and B) read "καυχησωμαι" "In order that I might boast." The reader of the apparatus will not fail to notice [that this is Origen's reading for the fifth column of the Hexapla]{.class_s1SV-0}. Pressed beyond measure, Nestle cannot put the Vatican reading into the text [because it doesn't make sense! ]{.class_s1SV-0}Rather than admit defeat and yield to the obvious truth that the Receptus is an older reading than the Hesychian, Nestle grabs frantically at "C" and writes "καυθησομαι" in the text. But "καυθησομαι" is the wrong spelling, for the word "καυθησωμαι" goes with "ινα" which, as any freshman student in Greek knows, is the subjunctive! Wrong ending! "καυθησωμαι" is the correct spelling; it stands in the Receptus as opposed [to A, Aleph, B, C, E, F, Tertullian,]{.class_s1SV-0} [Origen, and Nestle!]{.class_s1SV-0} When in doubt, throw the "new" Bibles out!

We shall now examine the pro-Catholic readings of the [ASV ]{.class_s1SV-0}and [RSV ]{.class_s1SV-0}as they return to the Latin Vulgate, via the Westcott and Hort "Greek" text.

II. Pro-Catholic Readings in the [ASV ]{.class_s1XK}(1901) and the [RSV ]{.class_s1XK}(1952).

One of the dictums used by Westcott and Hort for altering the Reformation text was that "doctrinal passages are suspect." In plain, crude, honest English this simply means that "any passage which clearly teaches correct Christian doctrine must have been interpolated by an Orthodox Christian for the purpose of getting the point across." (Such is the approach of the "neutral critic"!) This obligates him to erase such passages to prove that he (as any Agnostic, Infidel, or Atheist) is "neutral." But no Agnostic, Infidel, or Atheist is "neutral," and the Christian who assumes that God is [neutral ]{.class_s1SV-0}and would write a book which takes the [neutral point of view towards His Son(!) ]{.class_s1SV-0}is a Christian who is either as blind as a bat []{#cNE.xhtml_page_98}backing in backwards or he is in a wretched spiritual condition that would make Simon Peter's denial sound like an evangelistic invitation. Ignoramus or reprobate---either designation will fit the Westcott and Hort method of treating "doctrinal passages."

Rome is not "neutral" on "doctrinal passages."

Anyone who has studied the Catholic literature extensively knows the approach, attitude, motives, methods, and point of view taken by the hierarchy. We may excuse Westcott and Hort on the ground of ignorance, but we cannot excuse ourselves or John Huss (1369--1415) or Ian Paisley (Contemp.) or Savonarola (1452--1498) or Latimer (1485--1555) or Ridley (1500--1555) or the pitiful handful of Bible believers who have tried to preach the gospel in Spain since the Fascist Dictator Franco seized possession in 1939, with the blessing of Pope Pius XII.

The Bible is a book of [doctrine]{.class_s1SV-0}. As a matter of fact, that is the [first thing for which the Scriptures were inspired ]{.class_s1SV-0}(2 Tim. 3:16), and the young man entering the ministry is warned to pay attention to [doctrine ]{.class_s1SV-0}over and over and over again (1 Tim. 1:10, 6:1, 4:6, 6:3, 5:17; Titus 1:9). If "doctrinal passages" are "suspect," then [the whole Bible is "suspect." ]{.class_s1SV-0}The Westcott and Hort theory approaches the problem of "restoration of text" from the point of view of a detective who is suspicious of everyone in the house who might be guilty of murder, except Origen, Eusebius, etc.

In this case, the Bible (written by the Holy Spirit and preserved by that Spirit) is the culprit, and the "detective" is a man who accepts Origen's fifth column as the "purest text."

[A "detective" who attempts to alter "doctrinal passages" so that they become ]{.class_s1SU}[neutral passages ]{.class_s1SV-1}[is playing right into the hands of the greatest enemy of religious liberty that ever existed.]{.class_s1SU}[]{#cNE.xhtml_a1VY}[\[347\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1V7){.class_s1SX .noteref}[ For try as he may, the "detective" cannot alter some of the passages any other way than to make them fit the Roman system. This is perfectly apparent in what follows.]{.class_s1SU}

A. James 5:16. This is the passage used by the Catholic priest to prove that the confessional is a "Christian" institution. The Receptus didn't seem too pleased with this interpretation and was, therefore, careful to write "παραπτωματα" in the passage, instead of "τας αμαριας." That is, "faults," not ["sins."]{.class_s1SV-0} But what did the [ASV ]{.class_s1SV-0}(1901) []{#cNE.xhtml_page_99}do to the passage as its committee followed the "neutral" text of "purity"? they rewrote it as "τας αμαριας," exactly as the Vatican desired it to be written and read! [Is this the "neutral" point of view?]{.class_s1SV-0}

You say, "What is the manuscript evidence?" The evidence is not listed. In the footnotes (on p. 582 of Nestle's) you will find Aleph, B, and A [listed every time they appear anywhere in James 5:11--20, but they are NOT cited for James 5:16! ]{.class_s1SV-0}"τας αμαριας" is a Roman Catholic interpolation adopted by the [ASV ]{.class_s1SV-0}(1901) and the [RSV ]{.class_s1SV-0}(1952) to help the ecumenical movement along, and the [ASV ]{.class_s1SV-0}is just as corrupt as its cousin in this reading.

B. Matthew 23:14. There is no such thing as Matthew 23:14 in an [ASV ]{.class_s1SV-0}(recommended by the Bible faculties of Bob Jones, Dallas, Moody, Fort Worth, BIOLA, and Tennessee Temple schools). The [ASV ]{.class_s1SV-0}(1901), following the corrupt Westcott and Hort text, has omitted the whole verse. (Nestle omits it, also.) The [ASV ]{.class_s1SV-0}committee flippantly dismissed the verse with, "Some authorities insert . . . verse 14." "Some" is correct; [the majority insert it]{.class_s1SV-0}. However, the verse is not found in the Vulgate of Jerome, which followed Origen's fifth column. Was this passage "doctrinally suspect"? If so, who would have wanted it OUT?

Look at the verse!

"Woe unto you, scribes and Pharisees, hypocrites! for ye devour widows' houses, and for a pretense make long prayer: therefore ye shall receive the greater damnation."

Now reverse the field. Who could have wanted that verse [deleted? ]{.class_s1SV-0}(If you are truly "neutral" you always examine BOTH sides---right? If verses have been [added ]{.class_s1SV-0}because of doctrinal views, could they not also have [been taken out ]{.class_s1SV-0}because of doctrinal views?)

What we have here is someone protecting someone else from a Bible revelation that [contradicts their false doctrine. ]{.class_s1SV-0}Who in the world would be making "long prayers" for a "widow" and thereby getting her property? (You understand, of course, that the direct context, written by the Holy Ghost, is [a religious leader called "Father," do you not? ]{.class_s1SV-0}See Matthew 23:9. You do see it, don't you?) Now, how neutral can you be from here on?

The omission of Matthew 23:14 from the text of God's Holy word is neither an accident, nor the result of "scientific investigation," nor []{#cNE.xhtml_page_100}the result of an "objective approach." It is an Italian (Old Latin) and Roman (Vulgate) omission that is supported by the apostate Greek Scholars at Alexandria, Egypt. It was omitted for the same reason Acts 8:37 was omitted---[it was an offense to the Roman Catholic ecclesiastical system.]{.class_s1SV-0}

C. Matthew 6:7. In their zeal to produce a "neutral" text, Westcott and Hort now have to shut their eyes and ears from every fact of church history before, and during, the time in which they constructed their text. Here is a verse which reads, "Προσευχομενοι δε μη βατταλογησητε ωσπερ οι εθνικοι."
