The [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611 translates correctly, ["When ye pray, use not vain repetitions, as the heathen."]{.class_s1SW-0} The word "βατταλογησητε" means, basically, "to stammer" or "to repeat" the same thing over and over again. But my, how "doctrinally suspect" this reading is! How offensive to a "Christian" who stammered the same thing over and over again when he prayed! [Now who would object to "repetitions"? ]{.class_s1SV-0}Billy Sunday? Dwight Moody? General William Booth? George Muller? W.B. Riely?

Whoever it is, they need not fear a rebuke from the Bible for their sins if they will just buy a [Catholic Bible ]{.class_s1SV-0}(any edition) or an [RSV ]{.class_s1SV-0}(1952). The [RSV ]{.class_s1SV-0}[\
]{.class-0}(based on the Westcott and Hort text) translates [\
]{.class-0}"βατταλογησητε" as "heap up empty phrases"! With such a "Bible," who would ever get convicted for saying, "Hail Mary" or "Our Father" twenty times apiece while twiddling their beads?

D. Matthew 1:25. Here, the [AV ]{.class_s2HU}1611 (reading with the vast majority of manuscripts) has stated: "και ουκ εγινωσκεν αυτην εως ου ετεκεν τον πρωτοτοκον υιον." The last two words are the catch. In the [AV]{.class_s2HU}, this is "her firstborn son." The next to the last word---"πρωτοτοκον"---plainly being a combination of "proto"(first) and "teknon" (born). But the passages must be "doctrinally suspect" because the senile [ASV ]{.class_s2HU}(1901) along with the [RSV ]{.class_s2HU}(1952), has [removed the word "firstborn," ]{.class_s2HU}in keeping with the Alexandrian manuscripts.

But why the removal? Does not good old "D" (formerly used to offset A, Aleph, and B---see I., E., 3!) confirm the [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611 reading? Why the switch? Why was "πρωτοτοκον" removed?

It was removed from the [ASV ]{.class_s1SV-0}[]{#cNE.xhtml_page_101 .class-0}(1901) for the same reason it was removed from the Catholic Bibles; the word implies that Mary had other children [after ]{.class_s1SV-0}Jesus Christ (Mark 6:3), and Rome has always taught that Mary was a perpetual virgin (which means [that Joseph had to be a perpetual virgin, unless he stepped out on his wife!).]{.class_s1SV-0}

The "neutral text," created by Westcott and Hort, is, therefore, a text which removes verses on the Deity of Christ because they are "doctrinally suspect," [in line with Orthodoxy, ]{.class_s1SV-0}and then turns right around and removes verses which are offensive to Rome [because they expose her false teachings!]{.class_s1SV-0}

E. Matthew 6:13. All of the ending has been removed in the [ASV ]{.class_s1SV-0}(1901) so it will match the Roman Catholic Latin Bibles. Jerome removed ["For thine is the kingdom, and the power, and the glory, for ever . . ."]{.class_s1SW-0} for the simple reason that this was a Jewish prayer given to Jews who were under the Law [before the Crucifixion]{.class_s1SV-0}. Jerome (as Origen and Augustine) was Postmillennialist. (That simply means that he thought the world would get better and better till everybody became a Roman "Christian.") But in Postmillennialism you are taught to spiritualize Revelation 11:15 and omit the ["now"]{.class_s1SW-0} from John 18:36 (see the [Amplified Version]{.class_s1SV-0}, here) and change the tense of ["reign"]{.class_s1SW-0} (Rev. 5:10), Such a theology will not allow for a restoration of Israel or for the Kingdom returning to the ["king of the Jews"]{.class_s1SW-0} seated on the ["throne of David"]{.class_s1SW-0} to ["reign over the house of Jacob"]{.class_s1SW-0} (Matt. 19:28; Luke 1:30--33). Therefore, Matthew 6:13 must be altered so the "Kingdom" does not [return to Israel.]{.class_s1SV-0}

With this "neutral approach" (of a man who has spiritualized 500 verses in the Old Testament dealing with the restoration of Israel---see Rom. 11:25), Origen, Jerome, Augustine, Eusebius, Calvin, and Westcott and Hort (and the [ASV]{.class_s1SV-0}, 1901) tore the ending off of the prayer and "saved the day" for Postmillennial theology (remaining "neutral," of course!).

F. Matthew 19:17. This is the "stale crumb of Greek philosophy" mentioned in Chapter Five. The [ASV ]{.class_s1SV-0}(1901), along with its sister translation (the [RSV]{.class_s1SV-0}, 1952), preserves Origen's third-century Gnostic depravation for all to behold---"τι με ερωτας περι του αγαθου," "Why askest thou me concerning the good?" The correct reading is obviously "τι με λεγεις αγαθον ," []{#cNE.xhtml_page_102 .class-0}["Why callest thou me good?"]{.class_s1SW-0}

But when Origen hit the text, he lost his "neutral approach," for the text is one of the greatest in the New Testament on the depravity of man and the Deity of Jesus Christ. These are two "doctrinal subjects" which cannot be learned in any university or college. They are subjects of revelation by the Spirit of God; consequently, in no place in the Scripture is the spiritual ignorance of the [ASV ]{.class_s1SV-0}and [RSV ]{.class_s1SV-0}committees revealed any clearer than here. They bit at Origen's bait and in so doing they ignored ten fundamental facts of history and Christian doctrine.

1. No Orthodox Jewish "ruler" would waste five minutes discussing the "summum bonum" of the Greek philosophers.

2. The question in the text was about ETERNAL LIFE, not the "summum bonum!"

3. Any Jew who read his Scriptures knew what the "supreme good" was and would never have doubted this absolute standard for a moment.

4. Not even the questions of the Sadducees and Pharisees were philosophical questions---they were all questions about religious authority and fidelity to the Mosaic Law.

5. The young man is asking, ["What good thing shall I do?"]{.class_s1SW-0} Not, ["What is THE GOOD?"]{.class_s1SV-0}

6. The answer Jesus gives is a rebuke to the ruler's adjective in describing him (Jesus), ["Why callest thou me good?"]{.class_s1SW-0}

7. What follows is a statement to the effect that, "If I am not [good ]{.class_s1SV-0}I am not God, and if I am not God I am not good!" Note: ["There is none good but one, that is, God."]{.class_s1SW-0}

8. But oh! How this hurts the pride of an Alexandrian Greek scholar [who has castrated himself and gone barefoot to earn Heavenly merits!! ]{.class_s1SV-0}And oh! How this crucifies the pride of the men working on the ASV and RSV committees! ["There is none good but one, that is, God!"]{.class_s1SW-0}

9. [No man can remain neutral when dealing with the word of God]{.class_s1SV-0}[]{#cNE.xhtml_page_103 .class-0} (Matt. 12:25, 30; Rev. 3:15--16). In the next set of passages, the Roman Catholic Bible is usually truer to the Christian doctrine than the Protestant Bibles. In their efforts to sell books to "neutral" people, the "neutralists" have at last "neutralized" the God-breathed words of Divine Authority until there is nothing left but the man-breathed words of humanistic claptrap.

1. Luke 1:34. Here, the Greek text reads as the [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611 and the Latin Vulgate: "πως εσται τουτο, επει ανδρα ου γινωσκω," ["How shall this be, seeing I know not a man?"]{.class_s1SW-0} But marvel of marvels, here comes the [RSV ]{.class_s1SV-0}with ["Seeing I have no husband"!]{.class_s1SV-0}

What does this mean?

Are we to suppose that neither Mary nor Gabriel had enough sense to realize that a "single" woman could have a child?

What does a "husband" have to do with [bearing a child?]{.class_s1SV-0}

[Don't 30,000 women (or more) per year have children without having ]{.class_s1SU}[]{#cNE.xhtml_page_105}[husbands?]{.class_s1SV-1}

What is the manuscript authority for this quaint and archaic reading? [There is no manuscript authority]{.class_s1SV-0}. Every uncial or cursive manuscript which has the reading has it as found in the AV 1611. The Catholic Bible retains this correct reading, in spite of the fact that they would be tempted to drop it since it agrees with the Reformation text.

2. Luke 2:33. The God-honored text says: "και ην Ιωσηφ και η μητηρ αυτο," ["And Joseph and his mother."]{.class_s1SW-0} But someone wanted you to think that a medical physician (Dr. Luke) believed that Joseph was the real father of Jesus Christ! So the author of the fifth column of the Hexapla set the verse up for Eusebius to copy as "και ην ο πατηρ αυτου και η μητηρ." This time the Catholics bit at the bait when they should not have and accepted the heretical reading of the [ASV ]{.class_s1SV-0}(1901) which is recommended by the faculty members of the Conservative and Fundamental schools in the United States.

["His father and his mother"]{.class_s1SV-0} would not be the opinion of someone trying to protect someone else---as Luke 2:48 [plainly ]{.class_s1SV-0}is; it would have to be the Holy Spirit guiding the pen of the author of Luke's gospel. The reading is inexcusable, and a man who would adopt it is no more "neutral" than a rabbi shopping for groceries on the Passover. No Christian would have thought for a moment that Luke would recognize Joseph as the "father" of Jesus Christ, and a truly objective observer would have read Luke's account of Luke 1:29--35 and considered it when approaching a choice of manuscripts for the reading of Luke 2:33.

3. Acts 20:28. Here, again, the Roman reading is more Orthodox than the Protestant "Bibles." Where Rome has followed the Receptus of the [AV]{.class_s1SV-0}, 1611 Bible, they have read: "την εκκλησιαν του θεου, ην περιεποιησατο δια του ιδιου αιματος." But this reading is going to be hard for a neutralized, synthesized, objective, ecumenical integrator to stomach. For it states plainly:

\(1\) God has blood.

(2) He shed this blood for sinners.

(3) Saved sinners who make up His body were bought or purchased with this Divine Blood.

Now how can you reconcile a Universalist, Unitarian, Atheist, Liberal, Agnostic, Jehovah's Witness, or Buddhist (or Westcott and Hort) to [that?]{.class_s1SV-0}

You can't. So the [ASV ]{.class_s1SV-0}(1901), following the lead of Westcott and Hort, changes ["God"]{.class_s1SW-0} to "Lord" in the passage, and the other versions run riot in trying to avoid the nonneutral implications of the verse. Instead of the correct reading, ["The church of God, which he hath purchased with his own blood,"]{.class_s1SW-0} we find in the new versions, "Blood of his own," "Church of Jesus," "Blood of Jesus," etc. [anything except "God's blood"!]{.class_s1SV-0}

On this verse (Acts 20:28), the Roman Bibles remain true to the truth, but then in Colossians 1:14 and Acts 17:26 they get "cold feet" again, as the passage in Colossians says, ["through his blood,"]{.class_s1SW-0} and they would rather that it said ["through the mass."]{.class_s1SV-0}

Acts 17:26 is obviously a block to integration, so the word "blood" has been removed from it, exactly as you will find it [removed in the ASV (1901) ]{.class_s1SV-0}and the ["New" ASV]{.class_s1SV-0} (and the "brand, spanking, new, novel, up-to-date, latest [ASV," ]{.class_s1SV-0}and [any other "ASV").]{.class_s1SV-0}

4. John 9:35. The Catholic Bible has maintained the truth here as it is found in the [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611. The corrupt [ASV ]{.class_s1SV-0}(1901), however, has followed the reading of Origen's fifth column (incorrectly referred to as the "Septuagint"---see Chapter Four).

The reading is "συ πιστευεις εις τον υιον θεου." ["Dost thou believe on the son of God?"]{.class_s1SW-0} By some peculiar reasoning known only to a "neutral scholar," the verse has been altered to "συ πιστευεις εις τον υιον ανθροπου." But what does THAT mean? The only places in the Bible where Jesus Christ ever asked men to [believe on Him ]{.class_s1SV-0}were placed where He professed to be God's Son! (Note John 3:16, 3:36, 5:24, 3:17, 3:35, 6:40, 8:36, 11:4, 17:1, etc.) One of the great critical dictums for correcting the [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611 Greek manuscripts is that "one should always choose the language and expressions most characteristic of the author." Well, what in the world would possess a man who was acquainted with John's style (in the Gospels) to suddenly write "Son of MAN" where Jesus is dealing with a sinner on matters of [doctrinal belief? Is this characteristic of John? ]{.class_s1SV-0}It isn't in any twenty passages anywhere in the Gospel of John! ["The Son of God"]{.class_s1SW-0} is the correct reading and the [ASV, RV, RSV ]{.class_s1SV-0}and all the new "Bibles" are greatly in error, []{#cNE.xhtml_page_107 .class-0}["not knowing the Scriptures, nor the power of God."]{.class_s1SW-0}

5. John 3:16. The Latin Vulgate has at least retained "a form of godliness" in the verse, which has been abandoned by the [RSV ]{.class_s1SV-0}and many of the new translations. The word here is "μονογενη." Anyone can see at a glance that this is a compound word "mono" (one, only, or unique) and "gene" (generated, born). Yet, somehow, the [RSV ]{.class_s1SV-0}resents this compound word, so it divides the word in half and refuses to translate the second half of the word! Thus, God's ["only begotten"]{.class_s1SW-0} is reduced to "only." Someone resents God begetting a Son!

But it is no problem to find out who this "someone" is. For when the manuscript evidence is gathered, one will find that P66, P75, Vaticanus, and Sinaiticus (four manuscripts belonging to the same family!) have struck out the word "αυτου" in John 3:16, thus producing, ["God so loved the world that he gave only son,"]{.class_s1SV-0} instead of, ["God so loved the world, that he have HIS only begotten son."]{.class_s1SW-0} Since Griesbach's classification of manuscripts is set up on the theory that families have readings "characteristic of each other," the student should observe that [it is characteristic of the Alexandrian manuscripts to attack the Deity of Jesus Christ.]{.class_s1SV-0}

6. Mark 15:28. In spite of the [ASV's ]{.class_s1SV-0}overtures to Rome, the Catholic Bibles, up until 1950, still retain this verse (unless, of course, they are [RSV's)]{.class_s1SV-0}. The [ASV ]{.class_s1SV-0}(1901) strikes out the entire verse. The theory behind this is that Luke copied from Mark (and someone else), and Matthew copied from Mark (and someone else), and someone took Luke 22:37 out and stuck it back in Mark after Mark was finished. (This Liberal theory is based on the idea that no two writers in the Bible can agree in wording [unless they copied each other.)]{.class_s1SV-0}

The reading is found in the majority of uncials and cursives and it was deleted from Mark by someone who wanted to be a "Christian" [without being "numbered with the transgressors."]{.class_s1SV-0} (See I., F., above.)

7. Luke 9:55--56. Here the corrupt [ASV ]{.class_s1SV-0}(1901) follows Westcott and Hort "all the way," so to speak, and deletes twenty-eight words from the text. Over half of verse 55 and over half of verse 56 are []{#cNE.xhtml_page_108}subtracted from the Bible, leaving two short verses so ridiculously short that no one who read Luke would think that he wrote them. The following Bible verses in the English, ["But he turned, and rebuked them, and said, Ye know not what manner of spirit ye are of. For the Son of man is not come to destroy men's lives, but to save them. And they went to another village,"]{.class_s1SW-0} have been reduced to a Greek text reading, "στραφεις δε επετιμησεν αυτοις και επορευθησαν εις ετεραν κωμην," ["But turning he rebuked them, and they departed into another village."]{.class_s1SV-0}

But who would believe such a thing when he read the context? Look at verses 49, 50, 51, 52, 53, and 54. When Jesus rebuked the disciples in verse 50, did He not [SAY something ]{.class_s1SV-0}to them? Look at verses 57, 58, 59, 60, 61, and 62! Where are the verses that run only five words apiece? The [ASV ]{.class_s1SV-0}reading, as the readings of all the "new" Bibles, is obviously a dud. The Catholic Bibles (up to 1950) retain the true reading.

8. Luke 23:42. This is the most damaging evidence against the [ASV ]{.class_s1SV-0}(1901)---recommended by "Fundamentalists"---for in this reading the ancient Monarchian teaching is preserved which theorizes that the "Divine Christ" abandoned the "man-Jesus" when He was on the Cross. The Catholic Bibles from 500--1950 retain the correct reading which is the [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611 reading, "και ελεγεν τῳ Ιησου μνησθητι μου κυριε οταν." ["And he said unto Jesus, Lord, remember me when."]{.class_s1SW-0} This has been altered to "και ελεγεν Ιησου, μνησθητι μου οταν" in the [ASV ]{.class_s1SV-0}(1901), exactly as the Monarchian scribe altered the first copy he got his hands on between A.D. 150--300. ["And he said, Jesus, remember me ]{.class_s1SV-0}[\
]{.class-0}[when . . . ."]{.class_s1SV-0}

This remarkable corruption of text still stands in the ["New" ASV,]{.class_s1SV-0} to the shame and disgrace of the "Conservatives" who made the translation. The verse is so obviously an attempt to strip Jesus Christ of His Lordship that it is amazing that [any ]{.class_s1SV-0}Christian would have bought a copy of the [ASV ]{.class_s1SV-0}when it came out.

Not even the Roman Catholic versions (which changed the next verse into a reading that would deny "instantaneous salvation") took His Lordship from him in Luke 23:42. The [RSV ]{.class_s1SV-0}and the [ASV ]{.class_s1SV-0}both do this without apologies to anyone, and we certainly owe them no []{#cNE.xhtml_page_109}apologies here for their treatment of the Holy Bible.

The honest student should observe further that the deletion was not based on any manuscript evidence. There are [no manuscripts ]{.class_s1SV-0}which contain the [ASV ]{.class_s1SV-0}(1901) reading of Nestle and Westcott and Hort. The aborted text they present is arrived at by dropping the article "τῳ" in "και ελεγεν τῳ Ιησου," thus leaving "and he said" instead of ["And he said unto Jesus."]{.class_s1SW-0} This allows the Alexandrian and [ASV ]{.class_s1SV-0}textual critics (called "revisers") to make the word "Jesus" [part of the quotation]{.class_s1SV-0}. Hence, "And he said, Jesus . . . ." This [\
]{.class-0}Monarchian corruption is arrived at by taking the [\
]{.class-0}dative case of  ["]{.class_s1SV-0}Ιησου["]{.class_s1SV-0} and reading it as vocative. Since both endings "ου" are used in the vocative and the dative for the name [Jesus]{.class_s1SV-0} (Machen, [New Testament Greek for Beginners]{.class_s1SV-0}, pg. 188), the stunt is pulled off without a hitch. However, one critic did find the hitch. In the [Expositor's Greek Testament ]{.class_s1SV-0}(Nicoll, Eerdmans, Grand Rapids, Michigan, 1961), Alexander Bruce, from Glasgow, Scotland, spotted the corruption and noted (on page 641) that the reading of Aleph, B, and C (the "Big Three!") was produced by a "mistaken interpretation"! That is, where Aleph, B, and C contradict the [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611, someone has been [rewriting the Greek New Testament in the light of their own private interpretations of it.]{.class_s1SV-0}

This is a faithful saying and worthy of all acceptation.

These are a few brief samplings of comparisons of the Vulgate ([Rheims, Challoner]{.class_s1SV-0}, etc.) texts with the "new Bibles." On the whole, the Latin Vulgate was comparatively Orthodox when laid alongside the [RSV, ASV]{.class_s1SV-0}, or ["New English Bible,"]{.class_s1SV-0} Still, it is true that the [Challoner Rheims ]{.class_s1SV-0}edition of 1941 (Patterson, New Jersey) follows the readings of the [ASV ]{.class_s1SV-0}and [RSV ]{.class_s1SV-0}in Romans 8:1; Luke 2:14; Acts 1:3; John 3:13; Acts 8:37; John 18:36, 4:24; Revelation 22:19; Colossians 1:14, 2:12; I Timothy 6:20, 3:16; and Romans 13:9.

The most obvious corruption in the Catholic Bibles is the transposition of a comma in Hebrews 10:12 from after "forever" to a place after "sins." This "harmless change of punctuation," which could "not affect the text" (since anyone knows that the original manuscripts "were not punctuated," etc), leaves Jesus Christ sitting down [and never able to get up again!]{.class_s1SV-0}

"After he had offered one sacrifice for sins, sat down forever at []{#cNE.xhtml_page_110}the right hand of God."

But the reading is preposterous! The same Catholics who read this ridiculous alteration recite the "Apostle's Creed" in the same breath, which states that Jesus will [get up from His seat ]{.class_s1SV-0}and come again ["to judge the quick and the dead"!]{.class_s1SW-0} Either their creed or their Bible is hot air.

It is obvious that their Bible is the hot air, at least on this reading, for the comma was changed to protect the Roman Catholic mass! If the words were left standing as they are, the passage says, ["After he had offered one sacrifice for sins for ever,"]{.class_s1SW-0} but this is not good [Roman ]{.class_s1SV-0}doctrine.

In recent years, the Roman Church has adopted the [RSV ]{.class_s1SV-0}as their official Bible, plus (of course) the Apocrypha of Origen's fifth column. Its [fruits ]{.class_s1SV-0}are confusion, criticism, dead Orthodox profession, ritualism, sacra­mentalism, self-righteousness, pride, and apostasy; and not once in 1,900 years of church history has any revival, soul-winning effort, reformation, or revelation ever been connected with it. It is the Bible of the cloister, the council room, the theologian's study, the locked door, the clay urn, the mummy wrappings, and the secret conclave---it is not the living word of the living God, freely given to a fallen race. In this chapter, we shall see why the [AV]{.class_s1T2-0} 1611 English text is superior to the Westcott and Hort GREEK text. Our commendation of the [AV]{.class_s1T2-0} 1611 does not lie within the field of "literary beauty" or "graceful prose" or "poetic structure," but rather in the field of textual criticism: i.e., the English readings are superior to the Greek readings, which is born out by the comparison of one verse with another.

[1. Mark 1:2--3. Using Origen's corrupt "Septuagint," Eusebius, Augustine, and Jerome conjectured that the quotation which followed was from Isaiah the prophet.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cU6.xhtml_a1VN}[\[356\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1T9){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ Having made this conjecture, ]{.class_s1T0}[without reading Malachi,]{.class_s1T2-1}[ all of them changed the verse from "Καθως γεγραπται εν τοις προφηταις" to "Καθως γεγραπται εν τῳ Ησαιᾳ τῳ προφητῃ." Who can forget the corrupt reading of the RSV in Romans 5:1, ["Let us have peace," ]{.class_s1T2-0}which is based on Alexandrian (Aleph, A, B, []{#cU6.xhtml_page_124}and C) readings and Western (D) readings? While sneering at the "late manuscripts" used for ["we have peace"]{.class_s1T1-0} ([AV]{.class_s1T2-0} 1611), up popped the Wyman papyrus, the earliest known witness to Romans 4--5, with (guess what!) ["we have peace."]{.class_s1T1-0} The reading of the [AV]{.class_s1T2-0} 1611 was 150 years older than the archaic RSV reading.[]{#cU6.xhtml_a27A .class-0}[\[368\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2M6){.class_s1T7 .noteref}

And again, who can forget Westcott and Hort's monumental "boo-boo" in Matthew 27:34 when they amended this text to read ["wine mingled with gall,"]{.class_s1T2-0} while the [AV]{.class_s1T2-0} 1611 said ["vinegar to drink mingled with gall." ]{.class_s1T1-0}This is substituting "οινον" for "οξος." Doing their best to maintain a "neutral" position (upon behalf of the wine-drinking part of Christianity!), Westcott and Hort inserted the word "wine" into the text without even making a note of it in the appendix or apparatus of their edition (translation!). But no sooner had the text been invented than Dean Burgon (1896) produced a quotation of the text from Westcott and Hort's favorite "scholar"---Origen! Origen (bless his heart!) quoted the text (Matt. 27:34) from the Receptus he was mutilating, and not yet grasping the significance of the verse for wine drinkers (he was an abstainer), he let it stand as he quoted it in A.D. 230. The reading, 100 years [before]{.class_s1T2-0} Eusebius and Pamphilus wrote Vaticanus, was ["vinegar . . . mingled with gall,"]{.class_s1T1-0}[]{#cU6.xhtml_a1WH .class-0}[\[369\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1XJ){.class_s1T7 .noteref} [exactly as it stands in the AV 1611!]{.class_s1T2-0}

So don't get radically disturbed about fourteenth- and fifteenth-century manuscripts which contain the Johannine Comma.

Furthermore, we have seen the [AV]{.class_s1T2-0} 1611 correct errors of Greek manuscripts from the third and fourth centuries even in matters of canon. As a matter of fact, it is the [second edition]{.class_s1T2-0} of the [AV]{.class_s1T2-0} 1611 which drops the Apocrypha out altogether, not even including it in the space [between]{.class_s1T2-0} the Testaments. If the providential preservation of the true canon has been connected with the [AV]{.class_s1T2-0} 1611, why would it not be connected with a verse in that correct cannon?

(But these thoughts are not convincing to the Bible-rejecting "neutralist." He wants evidence on the text.)

The evidence that shows the passage should be there (if it was ever omitted) lies in the fact that [when the Johannine Comma is removed]{.class_s1T2-0} (part of verses 7 and 8), we get the following reading, which is grammatically impossible. "οτι τρεις εισιν οι []{#cU6.xhtml_page_125}μαρτυρυοντες, το πνευμα και το υδωρ και το αιμα, και οι τρεις εις το εν εισιν."

But Origen and Westcott and Hort never hesitated to violate the rules of freshman Greek grammar if it afforded an opportunity to destroy the despised Reformation text! (Note, for example, the [ASV]{.class_s1T2-0}, 1901, translation of 1 Tim. 3:16 on the Deity of Christ!)

The three words in verse 8 [retained by the new "Bibles" are "The spirit, and the water, and the blood." ]{.class_s1T2-0}But here, the Holy Spirit has pulled a neat trick on the grammarians, for all three of these words are listed as [neuter words]{.class_s1T2-0} in first-year elementary Greek grammar books. (Greek, as German, Spanish, and other languages, has "gender" in its noun endings.) Neuter nouns require neuter articles, normally. But the article in verse 8, [retained by the new "Bibles," ]{.class_s1T2-0}is [masculine]{.class_s1T2-0}. Thus, the "new Bibles" read, ["Because there are three (neuter) which bear witness . . . the spirit (neuter) the water (neuter), and blood (neuter) and these three (masculine!!) are in one."]{.class_s1T2-0}

Why would any man who professed to have passed Greek Grammar I maintain that such a reading was a "pure and neutral text"??

Something is missing from the text and the scholar!

This is what is missing; the only way that we can account for the [masculine]{.class_s1T2-0} use of three neuters in verse 8, is the fact that here [they have been "personalized."]{.class_s1T2-0} (That is, since all refer directly or indirectly to Jesus Christ Himself, they can be used as the "it" is used in Gen. 3:15 which see.) But the only way they could be "personalized" would be by retaining the reading of the [AV]{.class_s1T2-0} 1611, where all three words are [direct references to the Trinity]{.class_s1T2-0} (verse 7).

The surest proof that there is no other way to look at the problem is by the fact that 1 John 5:8 has been taught as a reference to [water baptism]{.class_s1T2-0} by the Romanists, Reformers, and Campbellites ever since they were old enough to read. Missing the connection entirely between 1 John 5:8 and 5:1, 4 and the water birth of John 3:4 which [is NOT baptism]{.class_s1T2-0}), the entire body of "Orthodox" scholarship has taught that the "water" of 1 John 5:8 was [baptism.]{.class_s1T2-0} Then, when they desired to revise the Bible in line with Alexandrian scholarship, they were confronted with the problem of the Johannine Comma (1881). []{#cU6.xhtml_page_126}They solved this problem by eliminating the "comma" and making the [water]{.class_s1T2-0} of 1 John 5:8 [personalized WATER!]{.class_s1T2-0}

If so, where is the "person"?

"The Person" [is in verse 7 of the AV 1611.]{.class_s1T2-0}

Moral: In exceptional cases, where the [majority of Greek manuscripts stand against the AV 1611, put them in file 13.]{.class_s1T2-0}

B. Mark 16:9--20. The passage has caused untold agony among those who have attempted to use it to teach Christian doctrines. Unable to "rightly divide" the passage (2 Tim. 2:15), Origen, Eusebius, and Westcott and Hort, etc., finally gave it up as a bad job and decided it never should have been in the Bible in the first place.

The Baptist reads it to verse 15, the Campbellite ventures to verse 16, the Holiness people launch out into verses 17 and 18, and then, in verse 20, the whole "cotton-pickin' thing" falls apart. You can't find an Apostle with the "signs" (2 Cor. 12:12) from Paul to Pope Paul---not even in the Mormon church!

[The definitive work on Mark 16:9--20 was written in 1871 by Dean Burgon, ]{.class_s1T0}[The Last Twelve Verses of the Gospel According to S. Mark]{.class_s1T2-1}[]{#cU6.xhtml_a28M}[\[370\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1Z0){.class_s1TN .noteref}[ ---and Westcott and Hort could not answer ]{.class_s1T0}[any of the arguments]{.class_s1T2-1}[ presented in it, so they ridiculed the good Dean and used "buffoonery" instead of logic to maintain their position.]{.class_s1T0}

Where most of the "new Bibles" dare not drop the entire passage, they at least put it in brackets or footnotes, and some of them drop it altogether.

As Dr. Hills has pointed out, the only thing that the critics agree on is that Mark 16:9--20 is not in Vaticanus and Sinaiticus. [How]{.class_s1T2-0} it was omitted, [why]{.class_s1T2-0} it was omitted, what [should have been there,]{.class_s1T2-0} and why [what now stands there]{.class_s1T2-0} (in the [AV]{.class_s1T2-0}) is wrong is something they don't seem to be able to talk about. (This is quite typical of the people who quote, "Judge not lest ye be judged," and deride a "negative" approach to Christianity. In a test case [which involves the word of God,]{.class_s1T2-0} they are the most destructive and negative people in the world. Why tear it down if you can't offer something better?)

Some say that Mark ended his gospel intentionally at verse 8. But when does the New Testament "good news" end on a negative note? It doesn't in Matthew, Luke, or John. It doesn't in Acts, Romans, Corinthians, or Ephesians. It doesn't in Galatians, Philippians, []{#cU6.xhtml_page_127}Colossians, or 2 Timothy. It doesn't in 1 Thessalonians, 2 Thessalonians, or Revelation. Why would anyone think that the first writer (most of the naturalistic critics say that Mark wrote first) ended with ["for they were afraid"]{.class_s1T1-0} (verse 8.)? Isn't this rather stupid?

Others say that Mark intended to finish his work but died at verse 8 and couldn't finish it. But Papias (A.D. 150), Clement of Alexandria (A.D. 200), and "good old Eusebius" and Origen say that Mark lived to publish it! (It's too late for Westcott and Hort to dump Origen and Eusebius now!)

[The third theory is that Mark 16:9--20 vanished into thin air. It was lost. It was torn out. It was burned. It was snipped out with a pair of scissors, etc. But as Creed (1930)]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cU6.xhtml_a29N}[\[371\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2EG){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ pointed out, how in the world did the "snip snapper" manage to tear the last twelve verses off 200 copies of Mark's gospel which were circulating all over Asia Minor, Italy, and Palestine? Not even Origen, with his fourteen stenographers and copyists, could have done that ---although he probably tried!]{.class_s1T0}

[But the evidence that the ]{.class_s1T0}[AV]{.class_s1T2-1}[ 1611 is the authentic reading is tremendous. As a matter of truth, it is so overpowering that one may disregard the Scofield note on Mark 16:8--9 without second thought.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cU6.xhtml_a1U6}[\[372\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2BF){.class_s1T7 .noteref}

The correct reading is found in every Greek manuscript in the world that contains Mark except Vaticanus and Sinaiticus. This ratio is better than 100 to 1. When any scholar says that "the better manuscripts" omit the passage, or "the oldest manuscripts" omit the passage, or "the verses from 9 on 'are not in the Greek,'" he is telling you that two manuscripts, [containing the Apocrypha]{.class_s1T2-0} (with Apocryphal books in the [New Testament)]{.class_s1T2-0}, are more authoritative than 200 Greek manuscripts which read as the [AV]{.class_s1T2-0} 1611!

In addition to this evidence are all the Syriac versions with the exception of the Sinaitic Syriac, all the Old Latin manuscripts except "k" (a close kin to Origen), and the verses are quoted by Hippolytus (200), Irenaeus (180), Tatian (175), and Justin Martyr (150). (The "k" manuscript has a spurious ending which would fool no one--- not even Westcott and Hort. It reads, "And all things whatsoever that []{#cU6.xhtml_page_128}had been commanded they explained briefly to those who were with Peter; after these things also Jesus Himself appeared and from the east unto the west sent out through them the holy and uncorrupted preaching of eternal salvation. Amen." This Latin innovation is the work of a papist trying to put Matthew 24:27 into the [past ]{.class_s1T2-0}and trying to promote the primacy of Peter over Paul.)

The [AV]{.class_s1T2-0} reading is the correct one, as usual.

C. John 7:53--8:11. The entire passage is knocked out of Nestle's text and Westcott and Hort rejected it as inspired literature. The [RV ]{.class_s1T2-0}and [ASV ]{.class_s1T2-0}put it in brackets; the [RSV ]{.class_s1T2-0}puts it in footnotes, and the [New English Bible]{.class_s1T2-0} tacks it on the end of John's gospel like a postscript.[]{#cU6.xhtml_a2GV .class-0}[\[373\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2N6){.class_s1T7 .noteref}

[Augustine did not like the passage, although he quotes it. Augustine chose the text of Origen's Hexapla, which excluded it.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cU6.xhtml_a1X3}[\[374\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a29X){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ Here, Jerome and Augustine had a falling-out; but this was due (as we have said before) to the fact that Augustine thought that "LXX" of ]{.class_s1T0}[A.D. 200]{.class_s1T2-1}[ was the inspired product of someone, somewhere, around ]{.class_s1T0}[250 B.C.]{.class_s1T2-1}[ Jerome (although he swallowed the legend of the mythological LXX) was leery of an "inspired" Greek Old Testament since he knew---as anyone should know---that the Old Testament was written in Hebrew. For this reason Jerome used the Hebrew text extensively in translating the canonical books. In Augustine's "Bible" there was a blank space between John 7:53 and John 8:11. True, it did make ridiculous reading; ]{.class_s1T0}[". . . art thou also of Galilee? Search and look; for out of Galilee ariseth no prophet. Then spake Jesus again unto them, saying . . . ."]{.class_s1T2-1}

That is, John must have been misled by the Holy Spirit, or the Holy Spirit got lost in the writing somewhere because in John 7:52 the scene is a discussion between Nicodemus and the Pharisees with the officers, and Jesus is [nowhere in the vicinity]{.class_s1T2-0} (note 7:32, 45). In John 8:12, Jesus is discoursing to the multitude in the presence of the Pharisees [in the treasury]{.class_s1T2-0} (8:20).

Origen's "Bible" reads rather stupidly, but it will not offend anyone who is worried about religious leaders committing adultery (!), for notice John 8:4---[where was the man? ]{.class_s1T2-0}The Levitical law does not require the adulteress to be stoned it requires the adulteress [and the adulterer to be stoned]{.class_s1T2-0} (Lev. 20:10)! If the [man]{.class_s1T2-0} in this case (John 8:7) was "caught in the act" (8:4), who could he have been []{#cU6.xhtml_page_129 .class-0}[but a Pharisee? ]{.class_s1T2-0}(See Luke 16:14--18, and notice the context.)

[I am afraid the passage is "doctrinally suspect." Jerome says the reading was in many Greek and Latin manuscripts ]{.class_s1T0}[before]{.class_s1T2-1}[ ]{.class_s1T0}[415,]{.class_s1T2-1}[]{#cU6.xhtml_a1XD}[\[375\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a225){.class_s1TN .noteref}[ and in the "Didache" (third century) and the Apostolic Constitutions (fourth century)]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cU6.xhtml_a25Y}[\[376\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a226){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ are found quotations from the ]{.class_s1T0}[AV]{.class_s1T2-1}[ 1611 passage. Eusebius (324), in his ]{.class_s1T0}[Ecclesiastical History]{.class_s1T1-1}[, gives extracts from a treatise by Papias (150) and notes that Papias recognized the story of the woman "accused before the Lord of many sins" as part of the Bible.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cU6.xhtml_a1TK}[\[377\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a227){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ Pacian (370) cites the passage, and the Montanists (second century) were aware of the passage and used John 7:53 in making additions to Acts 5:18.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cU6.xhtml_a23K}[\[378\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a228){.class_s1T7 .noteref}

[The ]{.class_s1T0}[RSV ]{.class_s1T2-1}[and the ]{.class_s1T0}[New English Bible]{.class_s1T2-1}[ have some very misleading notes in regard to this passage of Scripture, and they are well refuted by the work of Von Soden (1902). The misleading notes are based on the shallow and defunct observations of Westcott and Hort (Introduction, 1881) and Metzger (1964), which as usual, ignore the facts of church history.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cU6.xhtml_a2EE}[\[379\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2M3){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ Dr. Edward Hills goes into great length on the background of this verse and why it is missing from B, Aleph, L, W, P66, and P75. No decision made about John 7:53--8:11 could be an objective or "neutral" decision unless Dr. Hills' evidence]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cU6.xhtml_a2B7}[\[380\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2M4){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ is given consideration; his findings are a considerable advancement over the hundred-year old theory of Westcott and Hort.]{.class_s1T0}

(Two of the three remaining "disputed passages" are the ending on the Disciple's Prayer, commonly miscalled "The Lord's Prayer," and Matt. 19:17--19. We have already analyzed and discussed these in Chapter Seven, which see. The last passage remaining follows.)

[D. John 5:3b--4. Everything from ]{.class_s1T0}["waiting for the moving of the water"]{.class_s1T1-1}[ (verse 3) to ]{.class_s1T0}["whole of whatsoever disease he had"]{.class_s1T1-1}[ (verse 4) has been omitted in the "new" Bibles. The Alexandrian scribes (or scribe) deleted these verses, and their adulterations are visible in Aleph, B, and C manuscripts, plus the Sahidic, the Curetonian Syriac (corrupted by Origen during his stay in Caesarea),]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cU6.xhtml_a1VE}[\[381\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2GY){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ and a few Old Latin manuscripts.]{.class_s1T0}

[In spite of scholarship's opposition to the passage, R. Steck (1893), Henstsenberg (1875), and Hilgenfeld (1875) insist that the ]{.class_s1T0}[AV]{.class_s1T2-1}[ reading is correct.]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cU6.xhtml_a2H9}[\[382\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a21X){.class_s1T7 .noteref}

The reading is cited by Tertullian (A.D. 200) and Didymus (379) and Chrysostom (390), and is included in Tatian's Diatessaron, which was written [200 years before the Vatican manuscript was written.]{.class_s1T2-0}[]{#cU6.xhtml_a246 .class-0}[\[383\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1VD){.class_s1TN .noteref}[ ]{.class_s1T2-0}It is plain that the Alexandrian scribes, according to their usual habit, messed with the text, for "A" (as well as "L" ) has omitted half of verse 3 but [did not omit verse 4. ]{.class_s1T2-0}"D" and "W" omitted verse 4 but [left the last part of verse 3 as it is found in the Receptus!]{.class_s1T2-0} In spite of this obvious meddling, the passage has been preserved intact in the [AV]{.class_s1T2-0} 1611, and virtually intact in the vast majority of Greek manuscripts.

There are no other "highly doubtful" readings in the [AV]{.class_s1T2-0} 1611. Furthermore, the "highly doubtful" ones are not connected with the Deity of Christ. The verses studied here out of John chapter 5; John chapter 7; 1 John chapter 5; Matthew chapter 6; Matthew chapter 19; and Mark chapter 16 are quite unlike the "highly doubtful verses" of the Alexandrian manuscripts. The Alexandrian corruption's deal with the Deity of Jesus Christ and His Lordship, the infallibility of the Scriptures, the prophecies of the Second Coming and the truths of New Testament Salvation---1 Timothy 3:16; 2 Timothy 3:16; Luke 2:33; Acts 20:28, etc., etc.

The reader should observe that the outstanding "characteristic" of the "neutral text" is a Gnostic tendency to strip Jesus Christ of His Deity and the word of God of its authority. Study carefully the following references and note how the Alexandrian manuscripts [and the Bodmer III papyrus]{.class_s1T2-0} attack the Bible concept of Jesus Christ--- John 5:33, 18:37, 8:34, 16:8, 16:10, 6:69, 1:34; Colossians 2:9­--10; Romans 14:10; Mark 1:1; and Matthew 24:36. In all these readings, one will find that Aleph and B (and occasionally "C" and "D" ) take sides against any thought of magnifying Jesus Christ and giving Him the preeminent place (Col. 1:18), [which the entire Bible gives to Him. ]{.class_s1T2-0}They are "neutral" only in that they seek to [neutralize the person and work of the Lord Jesus Christ.]{.class_s1T2-0}

For this reason the [AV]{.class_s1T2-0} 1611 is a much better standard by which to judge the Greek text of Westcott and Hort than vice versa. Where the [AV]{.class_s1T2-0} says ["Jesus" ]{.class_s1T1-0}for Joshua (Acts 7:45; Heb. 4:8), it is pointing []{#cU6.xhtml_page_131}out that the book of Joshua is an accurate type of the Second Advent. (This is far above the "scientific exegesis" of Westcott and Hort or Origen or anyone like them in any century.) Where the [AV]{.class_s1T2-0} says ["be ye followers"]{.class_s1T1-0} instead of ["be ye imitators"]{.class_s1T2-0} (Eph. 5:1), it is correcting the error of the [ASV ]{.class_s1T2-0}(1901), for the translators of the [ASV ]{.class_s1T2-0}(1901) like Thomas A. Kempis and Sheldon believed that "imitating God" was "being a Christian." The Holy Spirit, knowing that the greatest "imitator" of God was Satan (See 2 Cor. 4:3--4, 11:10--14; Rev. 6:12, etc.), wrote, ["be ye followers." ]{.class_s1T1-0}If this is [not]{.class_s1T2-0} the Greek text, [the Greek text is wrong.]{.class_s1T2-0}

If the Greek text makes the mistake of writing the singular "KINGDOM" in Revelation 11:15 so that a Post-millennial fanatic could spiritualize it and say that Revelation 11:15 took place at the Ascension, the [AV]{.class_s1T2-0} 1611 irons out the problem with ["the kingdoms of this world" ]{.class_s1T1-0}so the reader can find the cross-reference to Luke 4:5 and Daniel 2:44 and get his eschatology straightened out!

If the Greek text has failed to put the word ["God"]{.class_s1T1-0} in Matthew 6:33 [where it belongs]{.class_s1T2-0}, it will show up in the [AV]{.class_s1T2-0} so the common layman can grasp the truth without the help of Greek scholarship. (The [ASV ]{.class_s1T2-0}reading here is Cyprian's and Eusebius' anyway!) If the Greek text has made the mistake of writing a word in Acts 4:27 which could be translated "servant" or "child," the Holy Spirit will resolve the ambiguity with ["thy holy child Jesus,"]{.class_s1T1-0} giving Him the preeminent place as God's Son, [not "servant"]{.class_s1T2-0} (as in the corrupt ASV, 1901).

[If, perchance, the Greek text fails to convey the truth that men have the same blood (Acts 17:26) and presents the "integrationist's" text]{.class_s1T0}[]{#cU6.xhtml_a2FY}[\[384\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a224){.class_s1T7 .noteref}[ by omitting the word "blood," the Holy Spirit is careful to preserve the scientific truth of the matter with ]{.class_s1T0}["and hath made of one blood"]{.class_s1T1-1}[ (Acts 17:26). This is the reading of the ]{.class_s1T0}[AV]{.class_s1T2-1}[ 1611, which can be used to critique the contaminated Greek manuscripts.]{.class_s1T0}

If, by chance, the Greek allows a scholar to exempt himself from the charge of Romans 1:18 on the grounds that he is not "hindering" the truth or "preventing the spread of the truth," the [AV]{.class_s1T2-0} 1611 puts the accent in the right place and states that the wrath of God is revealed from Heaven against ["men, who hold the truth in unrighteousness."]{.class_s1T1-0} Since all textual critics and revisers [hold the truth]{.class_s1T2-0}[]{#cU6.xhtml_page_132 .class-0} when they mutilate it, the shoe fits: wear it.

If the polluted Greek manuscripts forget to finish Romans 8:1 and it is removed in the [ASV ]{.class_s1T2-0}and similar polluted "Bibles," the Holy Spirit will preserve it in the [AV]{.class_s1T2-0} 1611, since it matches verse 4 and verse 13 anyway in the context. There IS condemnation for a Christian who "walks in the flesh," and this is apparent from Romans 8:13. There is no [eternal]{.class_s1T2-0} condemnation, but Romans 8:1--13 is not dealing with eternal condemnation and any simpleton can see that without a high school education.

If the Greek doesn't have enough sense to include ["thou shalt not bear false witness"]{.class_s1T1-0} in Romans 13:9, the [AV]{.class_s1T2-0} 1611 will insert it where it belongs, and those who [bore false witness]{.class_s1T2-0} (when they left this out in the [ASV]{.class_s1T2-0}, 1901) can bear their own judgment. Where the Greek says one thing and the [AV]{.class_s1T2-0} says another, throw out the Greek.

If any Greek manuscript should make the mistake of putting ["we shall reign"]{.class_s1T1-0} into the third person, plural, present indicative active, the [AV]{.class_s1T2-0} 1611 will correct it, exactly as it did the private interpretation of the verse found in the [ASV ]{.class_s1T2-0}(1901), "they reign." This is a Post­millennium addendum and it is derived from a doctrinal bias which accepts Augustine's ["City of God"]{.class_s1T2-0} as Bible doctrine.[]{#cU6.xhtml_a1YF .class-0}[\[385\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1YG){.class_s1T7 .noteref}

If the Greek text implies, "Abstain from every form of evil" (1 Thes. 5:22), the [AV]{.class_s1T2-0} 1611 narrows the meaning of the exact warning, ["Abstain from all appearance of evil." ]{.class_s1T1-0}You can abstain from all [forms]{.class_s1T2-0} without abstaining from the "appearance," and this is apparent to any Christian. Whoever changed the verse in the [ASV ]{.class_s1T2-0}(1901) undoubtedly had a motive for doing it; and they did the same thing in 1 Timothy 6:10 when they claimed that the love of money was not ["the root of all evil,"]{.class_s1T1-0} but only ["a root of all kinds of evil." ]{.class_s1T2-0}One can see at a glance that the [AV]{.class_s1T2-0} has been a ["discerner of the thoughts and intents of the heart"]{.class_s1T1-0} (Heb. 4:12) of the [ASV ]{.class_s1T2-0}committee, and it has flushed the covey! What scholars do [with]{.class_s1T2-0} the [AV]{.class_s1T2-0} text [reveals how they feel about being rebuked for their sins.]{.class_s1T2-0}

Where the perverse Greek reads one way and the [AV]{.class_s1T2-0} reads the other, rest assured that God will judge you at the Judgment on what you know. Since you don't know the Greek (and those who knew it altered it to suit themselves), you'd better go by the [AV]{.class_s1T2-0} 1611 text.

# [Chapter 9 - ]{.class_s1WA}[]{#cYJ.xhtml_page_134}[Bamboozling the Elect]{.class_s1WB} {.heading_s3E-2}

[In Matthew 24:4, 11, 24, the Lord Jesus Christ gives some warnings, and although we understand that these warnings were given primarily to Israel in the Tribulation, there are so many references like them ]{.class_s1SU}[aimed at the Christian ]{.class_s1SV-1}[that we may well observe those of Matthew chapter 24 as signposts on the highway home to glory.]{.class_s1SU}[]{#cYJ.xhtml_a22R}[\[386\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2MU){.class_s1SX .noteref}

These Biblical "red lights" are set in the Scripture for a purpose. Whether or not the textual critics, Bible revisers, manuscript "detectives," etc., pay any attention to them is immaterial. The Christian [must pay attention to them ]{.class_s1SV-0}or suffer the consequences. The three most outstanding warnings given to the Body of Christ by the Apostle to the Gentiles---who was given the revelation of the Mystery of the Body---are in 1 Timothy 6:20 and Colossians 2:8. These three warnings are found in "prison epistles" written near the end of Paul's life. They warn the Christian to look out for three things mainly; but Augustine, Jerome, Origen, Eusebius, Westcott and Hort, Scofield, Warfield, Machen, and Robertson paid no more attention to these warnings than if they had never been written.

The three salient enemies (in addition to "the rudiments of this world"---Col. 2:8) for which the Christian is to be on guard against are:

1\. SCIENCE.

2\. PHILOSOPHY.

3\. TRADITIONS OF MEN.

Here the Holy Spirit has guarded His own work from being destroyed, for these three "false gods" are the bedrock foundation of the Westcott and Hort Greek text. Defending Satan on these grounds, the dead Orthodox Christian replies:

1. The word "science" really means "knowledge," and knowledge is good; the only thing forbidden is "false knowledge." (An anti-Communist "crusader" who operates out of New Jersey recently made the statement, "[God]{.class_s1SV-0} and science are ONE!" This was made over a national hookup of more than 100 stations.)

[To all of this hogwash it may be replied: There is correct knowledge which ]{.class_s1SU}[does no good at all]{.class_s1SV-1}[,]{.class_s1SU}[]{#cYJ.xhtml_a2FT}[\[387\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2AV){.class_s1SX .noteref}[ and there is a wisdom which is Satanic.]{.class_s1SU}[]{#cYJ.xhtml_a26Z}[\[388\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2AW){.class_s1SX .noteref}[ The word "science" today is a word that really can be applied only to knowledge ]{.class_s1SU}[that deals with phenomena in the physical realm]{.class_s1SV-1}[.]{.class_s1SU}[]{#cYJ.xhtml_a1TE}[\[389\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2AX){.class_s1SX .noteref}[ Further, the words "Gnostic" and "Gnosis" are the Greek words for "science," and this clearly places the first century warning in the lap of the ]{.class_s1SU}[college at Alexandria.]{.class_s1SV-1}[]{#cYJ.xhtml_a25D}[\[390\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2AY){.class_s1UE .noteref}

2. The word "philosophy" simply means "some man's individual philosophy" or "outlook on life," not the [subject ]{.class_s1SV-0}itself.

[To which it may be replied: No Greek manuscript (uncial or cursive, Alexandrian, Western, or Syrian) has the reading ]{.class_s1SU}["HIS philosophy"]{.class_s1SV-1}[ in it; this reading is, therefore, an invention of a philosopher who wanted to retain his idol. A "lover of wisdom" (Greek---"φιλοσοφια") is not always a ]{.class_s1SU}[lover of God]{.class_s1SV-1}[, for there are ]{.class_s1SU}[two kinds of wisdom]{.class_s1SV-1}[]{#cYJ.xhtml_a2A5}[\[391\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2H5){.class_s1UE .noteref}[ pointed out in a King James Bible. The outstanding mark of the wrong kind]{.class_s1SU}[]{#cYJ.xhtml_a2JB}[\[392\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2H6){.class_s1SX .noteref}[ is a lack of the "fear of God"]{.class_s1SU}[]{#cYJ.xhtml_a2D4}[\[393\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2H7){.class_s1SX .noteref}[ and a desire to seek "wisdom" ]{.class_s1SU}[instead of Bible truth]{.class_s1SV-1}[]{#cYJ.xhtml_a2D1}[\[394\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2H8){.class_s1UE .noteref}

3. The word "traditions" is not to be "crucified," for did not Paul ask the Christians to remember them in 2 Thessalonians 2:15?

To which it may be replied: The traditions of 2 Thessalonians 2:15 are those of 2 Thessalonians 3:6--14 (in the context!) and are not in the least to be connected with the traditions of Westcott and Hort or the Roman Catholic Popes, i.e., a Septuagint written in Alexandria that was a "Christian's Bible," a rescission of the "original" at Antioch by Lucian, Herod's [daughter ]{.class_s1SV-0}doing a belly dance (instead of his [wife's daughter]{.class_s1SV-0}), Vaticanus being a neutral text, the dying thief saying "Jesus" instead of "Lord," Mary's immaculate conception, her Assumption, Papal infallibility, transubstantiation, mass, "sacraments," and all the other depraved Babylonian nonsense.

In short, the dead Orthodox Christian always takes a cheerful, optimistic view about [negative warnings ]{.class_s1SV-0}which deal with him and his fellow man. This is the standard Liberal view, and many "Orthodox" Christians who believe in the "fundamentals of the faith" are [Liberal in their approach to the Scriptures from whence the fundamentals are derived.]{.class_s1SV-0}

[It is certain (independent of anyone's opinion or authority) that Satan is interested in the ]{.class_s1SU}[spoken ]{.class_s1SV-1}[and ]{.class_s1SU}[written ]{.class_s1SV-1}[]{#cYJ.xhtml_page_136}[word of God (Gen. 3, Luke 4) and that neither time nor circumstance has changed his attitude ]{.class_s1SU}[or approach ]{.class_s1SV-1}[toward the Scriptures.]{.class_s1SU}[]{#cYJ.xhtml_a2GD}[\[395\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1YC){.class_s1SX .noteref}

[With this in mind, the consistent Bible-believing Christian will study carefully the ]{.class_s1SU}[methods and motives ]{.class_s1SV-1}[involved in the 20th century attack on the Authorized Version and will certainly not be so gullible or so naive as to think that he is dealing with honest and impartial men simply because they profess to be "neutral" where the Deity of Christ and the inspiration of the Scriptures are concerned.]{.class_s1SU}[]{#cYJ.xhtml_a1ZM}[\[396\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a22K){.class_s1SX .noteref}

The modern reviser is located, identified, described, judged, and condemned in the following passages which were preserved in a text that revisers would not have thought to meddle with until [after ]{.class_s1SV-0}it was declared canonical and fixed---the Old Testament in Hebrew!

These passages declare that there ARE "revision committees" (if the shoe fits, wear it!) who:

1. Are composed of men who are afraid of the results of street preaching (Jer. 36:10, 16; John 11:47--48). And---

2\.  They resent the fact that the spoken word is for the common "man in the street" (Jer. 36:6, 10, Acts 5:28, 40).

3. They worried about the political consequences of a message that destroys "unity" (Jer. 38:4; John 11:47--48).

4. They are usually high up in the political world and have "mixed motives" in regard to Bible translations (Jer. 38:4--5, 36:16, 20).

5. They have access to the true Scriptures, as anyone else does (Jer. 36:11, 13; Isa. 45:19).

6. They do NOT fear and tremble at the reading of the true word of God (Jer. 36:24), whereas, a real believer will every time (2 Chron. 34:26--27).

7\.  They are noted for "shorter readings" which are arrived at by [cutting the verses out ]{.class_s1SV-0}(Jer. 36:23)!

8. They have an affinity [for Egypt ]{.class_s1SV-0}and trust Egyptian scholarship and military power (Jer. 41:17, 42:1--4; 43:1--4).

9. They are optimistic about world peace (Jer. 23:16--17) []{#cYJ.xhtml_page_137}and speak of it frequently (Ezek. 13:7, 16).

10. They are DEISTS in their approach to translating. They assume that all similarities in verses are due to copying and that there is no such thing as a book written under inspiration without a reference to some other book (Jer. 43:2--3). To them, God is "out of the question" when it comes to [preservation]{.class_s1SV-0}, and they feel free to handle His writings as they see fit (Ezek. 8:12).

11. They can be spotted in any generation by a smooth, slick, scholarly vocabulary, and the adoption and use of words that are not in the Bible vocabulary but are in "university vocabularies" of the day and age in which they live (Rom. 16:18; Jude 16).

12. Their revisions are attempts to rid the world of the word under the hypocritical pretense of "seeking to restore the originals" (note Jer. 36:17)!

The last point brings us to the point of this chapter. In view of all the nonscholarly, nonobjective, nonneutral phenomena described in the last two chapters, what exactly [is the reason ]{.class_s1SV-0}for changing the [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611? We know the reasons [given for changing it]{.class_s1SV-0}, but what are the reasons actually? (The reasons [given ]{.class_s1SV-0}are given so as to allow a loophole for anyone wishing to alter the Bible text.)

The first reason which will allow the reviser to change the [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611 is: "The version is archaic; it needs to be brought up-to-date." But where the "new Bibles" confuse a passage and mess it up[]{#cYJ.xhtml_a2AN .class-0}[\[397\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a20G){.class_s1SX .noteref} (to where you can [not ]{.class_s1SV-0}understand it as well as it appears in the [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611), [then the "reason" switches! ]{.class_s1SV-0}Now it is, "This reading is [more accurate ]{.class_s1SV-0}than the [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611!"

With this double standard (a convenient expedient for the double-tongued if you ever saw one!), the [RV, ASV, RSV, New English Bible, ]{.class_s1SV-0}Mickey Mouse[, Amplified]{.class_s1SV-0}, Weymouth, Charlie Brown, Goodspeed, Berkeley, Phillips, Dick Tracy, Montgomery, etc., go sailing off through the word of God tearing it to pieces.

If it is plain, [change ]{.class_s1SV-0}it and make it more "accurate." If it is accurate, [change ]{.class_s1SV-0}it and make it "plainer."

If it is plain, ["God was manifest in the flesh,"]{.class_s1SW-0} make it more "accurate"---["He who was manifest in the flesh."]{.class_s1SV-0} If it is accurate, []{#cYJ.xhtml_page_138 .class-0}["To whom he showed himself alive after his passion by many infallible proofs," ]{.class_s1SW-0}then make it "plainer"---["many convincing demonstrations."]{.class_s1SV-0} But who is trying to kid who? Jeremiah told us all about these people who pervert ["the words of the living God"]{.class_s1SW-0} (Jer. 23:36) under the guise of "liberating the Bible from its ancient clothing of archaic English," etc. What happened when Eisenhower "liberated" Arkansas? What happened when Hitler "liberated" Czechoslovakia? What happened when Russia "liberated" Hungary? What happened when Castro "liberated" Cuba? What happened to France when she became "liberated" from the Bible and the truth?

First, we present for the reader's indulgence a few samples of the need for "revision" of the [AV]{.class_s1SV-0}. Following this we offer a few samples of the "better substitutes" that have been proposed for the [AV. ]{.class_s1SV-0}Then, as exhibit C, we will give a list showing how 24 versions have been deceived into adopting the reading of the Latin Vulgate (A.D. 405!) instead of the "original" Greek of the [Authorized Version ]{.class_s1SV-0}(A.D. 1611).

I. Archaic words (or mistaken words) that need "updating."

[Among these are included "aforetime," "howbeit," "peradventure," "thee," and "thou."]{.class_s1SU}[]{#cYJ.xhtml_a1VX}[\[398\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1Y8){.class_s1SX .noteref}[ These are to be replaced.]{.class_s1SU}

[What happens? The ]{.class_s1SU}[RSV ]{.class_s1SV-1}[replaces "thee" and "thou" with YOU where it refers to Jesus Christ, but retains "thee" and "thou" where it refers to the Roman Whore of Revelation chapter 17! This is all done with the most cherubic demeanor, while stating that the terms "thee" and "thou" have been "reserved for Deity"!]{.class_s1SU}[]{#cYJ.xhtml_a1U5}[\[399\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2C7){.class_s1SX .noteref}[ If this is the type of thing that occurs when "archaic words" are removed or replaced, it can just as well be dispensed with. Perhaps the ]{.class_s1SU}[RSV ]{.class_s1SV-1}[committee worships the WHORE on the Seven Mountains, but the Bible-believing Christian does NOT.]{.class_s1SU}

It is pointed out that "communicate" meant "to share" in the days of the [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611, not "to talk."[]{#cYJ.xhtml_a21U .class-0}[\[400\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2G7){.class_s1SX .noteref} The reader will find the [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}uses the word [both ways]{.class_s1SV-0}---see Galatians 6:6 and Luke 24:17.

[It is pointed out that "let" means to "hinder,"]{.class_s1SU}[]{#cYJ.xhtml_a22C}[\[401\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a21C){.class_s1SX .noteref}[ but this is stupidity on the part of the objector. Nowhere in the ]{.class_s1SU}[AV ]{.class_s1SV-1}[in 1 Corinthians 6:17; 1 Corinthians 14:39--40; Ephesians 5:3; Philippians []{#cYJ.xhtml_page_139}4:5; Colossians 2:16; or 2 Thessalonians 2:3 does it ever mean "hinder." It means "hinder" in Isaiah 43:13; Romans 1:13; and 2 Thessalonians 2:7. The ]{.class_s1SU}[AV ]{.class_s1SV-1}[uses the word ]{.class_s1SU}[both ]{.class_s1SV-1}[ways, and the context will determine the meaning. Not only this, but the biggest objectors to "let" are the Fundamentalists who didn't like it standing in 2 Thessalonians 2:7. What is the point of correcting it in the "new" Bibles when all the new Bibles are put out by ]{.class_s1SU}[Post-millennialists and Amillennialists who never believed the passage in 2 Thessalonians literally to start with! ]{.class_s1SV-1}[What is the point?]{.class_s1SU}[]{#cYJ.xhtml_a2MR}[\[402\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a21D){.class_s1SX .noteref}

It is called to our attention that the "which" of Philippians 4:13 should be translated "who." But no sooner do the "liberating-up-to-daters" get to work on the "which" than they [take the word "Christ" clean out of the passage! ]{.class_s1SV-0}What advantage is gained by translating "which" as "who" and then taking the "who" slap out of the verse?! Do you think everyone is as stupid as YOU are?

[It is objected that "Areopagus" and "Mars Hill" (Acts 17:19, 22) are the same word and, therefore, it should not have two translations. If it should not have two translations, why is it "Mars Hill" in Alford's translation]{.class_s1SU}[]{#cYJ.xhtml_a2D5}[\[403\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2H0){.class_s1SX .noteref}[ and "the City Auditorium" (!) in William's translation?]{.class_s1SU}[]{#cYJ.xhtml_a2AJ}[\[404\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2H1){.class_s1SX .noteref}[ Isn't "Chicago" translated "Chi" and the "Windy City"? Isn't New York "Gotham"? ]{.class_s1SU}[What is the problem?]{.class_s1SV-1}

II\. Mistakes in translating.

The [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}has mistranslated 1 Corinthians 4:6. It should have been ["Learn by us to live according to Scripture" (RSV).]{.class_s1SV-0} But what man who can read sixth-grade English would have any trouble with the verse! Because the scholars could not find "what was written"[ (AV,]{.class_s1SV-0} ["Above that which is written"),]{.class_s1SW-0} they altered the verse to mean "keep within the rules" [(New English Bible)]{.class_s1SV-0} and other readings which would indicate that Paul had suddenly quit discussing the problem of "personalities" and had switched to "rules for Christian living." But these "new" readings are private interpretations divorced from context, for the subject of 1 Corinthians 4:6 is "judging ministers by their appearance and reputation" (verses 1, 3--5). All Paul said, in effect, was, "I am including myself with everybody else until the Judgment Seat of Christ, and that goes for Apollos, too. Don't look on us as "big shots' because what is written [(the Scriptures on Judgment, naturally! verse 5)]{.class_s1SV-0} includes all men as sinners." []{#cYJ.xhtml_page_140 .class-0}[(How's that for a "new English translation"?)]{.class_s1SV-0} The [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611 is just about twice as clear as either the [RSV ]{.class_s1SV-0}or the[ "New" English Bible.]{.class_s1SV-0}

Further objections: The "numbers" are wrong in the [AV. ]{.class_s1SV-0}For example, 1 Kings 9:28 says 420, but 2 Chronicles 8:18 says 450! On this basis, we are asked to put our [AV's ]{.class_s1SV-0}in the wastebasket (where the [RSV ]{.class_s1SV-0}already is!). How do you know there weren't two [different trips? ]{.class_s1SV-0}Was Ophir so far off that Solomon only got one boat load in 40 years? [He reigned 40 years]{.class_s1SV-0}. He had a "navy." Why did all the gold have to be on [one boat?]{.class_s1SV-0} Why not 420 on one and 450 on another? If the chronicler of Kings is the main chronicler for Israel, and the chronicler of Chronicles is the main one for Judah, couldn't they have received a different report? Would not 450 [include ]{.class_s1SV-0}420? Isn't this the same problem as the inscriptions on the cross? And if it isn't, why is the [Authorized Version ]{.class_s1SV-0}never given the benefit of a doubt that is given to Septuagints, "LXX's," Hexaplas, and Westcott and Hort texts?

More objection: The [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}fails to preserve the gender of nouns and the tense of verbs. One would think that the "them" of Matthew 28:19 was [nations ]{.class_s1SV-0}instead of [individuals ]{.class_s1SV-0}because the syntax of αυτους has not been preserved---it is masculine and "nations" is neuter. The "commit" of I John 3:9 should have been "continually practices" (Greek: ποιει) and without this present, indicative active (linear), the verse will be "misinterpreted," etc.

But is the case really that "tough"?

Has anyone ever seen a "nation" that wasn't a group of individuals? How would one "baptize a nation" without baptizing individuals? Not even the Pope would try that one, and he would baptize bells, fishing boats, dog houses, and bathrooms! (They sprinkle them just like they do babies!)

[If the Greek syntax was preserved ]{.class_s1SV-0}according to the scholars wish, what would you do with this? "Προ δε της εορτης του πασχα ειδως ο Ιησους οτι ηλθεν αυτου η ωρα ινα," ["Before but of the feast of the passover, having known the Jesus that He came of him the hour in order that"]{.class_s1SV-0} (John 13:1). What would God do with a translation like that but put it in the garbage can with the twentieth-century translations?

And does the "linear tense" solve the problem of 1 John 3:9? (Kenneth Wuest got hung up on this kick in his writings and wound up having to put the "linear" tense in every time. He wound up with salvation conditioned on "keep on practicing righteousness" (1 John 3:10), and anyone was given the leeway of breaking the law once, as long as they didn't "continually transgress the law" (1 John 3:4). No, the answer to 1 John 3:9 is [in the English of John 3:6]{.class_s1SV-0}. The text is dealing with the part of a man that is born again, not on the conduct of a Christian who sins occasionally but not habitually. (A little English will clear up the obscurities of any Greek text.)

[It is objected that the word "suffer" should be "allow." Should it really? Would any man ]{.class_s1SU}[now ]{.class_s1SV-1}[say, "ALLOW the little children to come unto me" (Matt. 19:14)? Would he not say, "LET the little children ]{.class_s1SU}\
[. . ."? But if Jesus had said, "Let," in the ]{.class_s1SU}[AV ]{.class_s1SV-1}[1611, the critics would have said it means "prevent"! ]{.class_s1SU}[(They just said it.)]{.class_s1SV-1}[]{#cYJ.xhtml_a1Y3}[\[405\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1YJ){.class_s1UE .noteref}

The [RSV ]{.class_s1SV-0}puts "let" in this passage (Matt. 19:14) and then [inserts Origen's Gnostic depravation two verses later! ]{.class_s1SV-0}This is the price the Bible believer is asked to pay to get "allow' or "let" instead of "suffer." (You are a fool if you are willing to pay it.)

"Suffer" implies that it will [cost you something ]{.class_s1SV-0}and you will have to "put up" with some privation to allow certain things to come to pass. It is a good word, and if the price of dropping it is a Socratic dialogue in the middle of the New Testament, the Socratic dialogue can go home to Hell with the [ASV ]{.class_s1SV-0}that reproduced it.

[It is objected that "Hell" (for "Hades" and "Gehenna") is improper. To correct this "error," the new Bibles read "Hades" for "hell" in a dozen places,]{.class_s1SU}[]{#cYJ.xhtml_a2J4}[\[406\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1WR){.class_s1SX .noteref}[ and the guileless Christian is told this a better "translation."]{.class_s1SU}[]{#cYJ.xhtml_a1ZN}[\[407\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a1WS){.class_s1SX .noteref}[ But Hades ("αδης") is not a ]{.class_s1SU}[translation, it is a TRANSLITERATION. ]{.class_s1SV-1}[By the use of this transliteration, the word "Hell" has been all but taken out of the Bible, much to the delight of Christ-rejecting, self-righteous "Christians." If the revisers had been honest men, would they not have transliterated "Heaven" as well and called it "Ouranos" (Greek: "ουρανος") instead of "Heaven"? Again, if they wanted to put the Bible "in the language of twentieth-century people," why did they not invent a NEW word for "Hades"? ]{.class_s1SU}[Hades is NOT an English word.]{.class_s1SV-1}

It is objected that the word "Jeremiah" has been transliterated three different ways in the [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611 (Matt. 27:9, 16:14, and 2:17). This is "confusing to the reader." It didn't confuse Moody, Torrey, Finney, Sunday, Spurgeon, Scofield, Carey, Goforth, Livingstone, DeHaan, Fuller, Ironside, Rice, or anyone wise who believed the Bible and [put it into practice. WHOM DID IT "CONFUSE"? ]{.class_s1SV-0}If the new Bibles are going to clear up these "inconsistent practices," how is it that they have translated the word "Alma" (Hebrew) three different ways, while spelling Jeremiah the same way every time?[]{#cYJ.xhtml_a1YE .class-0}[\[408\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2N8){.class_s1SX .noteref} Are we supposed to be so stupid as to imagine that the word for "Virgin" (Alma), referring to the Virgin Birth of Jesus Christ, is of [less importance ]{.class_s1SV-0}than the transliteration of a proper name given to a prophet?

[Why did not Westcott and Hort preserve the correct spelling of Nebuchadnezzar?]{.class_s1SU}[]{#cYJ.xhtml_a2JT}[\[409\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2E4){.class_s1SX .noteref}[ It is found in the book of Daniel, and the book of Daniel is found extracted from the "LXX" (A.D. 150--370) and placed in Vaticanus! Didn't Westcott and Hort observe ]{.class_s1SU}[in their favorite manuscript ]{.class_s1SV-1}[that the name had to be transliterated ]{.class_s1SU}[six different ways? ]{.class_s1SV-1}[Someone is a little deficient in "accredited scholarship."]{.class_s1SU}

[It is objected that in Mark 6:20 the reading should be "kept him safe," instead of ]{.class_s1SU}["observed him."]{.class_s1SW-1}[ Out come the pens,]{.class_s1SU}[]{#cYJ.xhtml_a20H}[\[410\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a248){.class_s1SX .noteref}[ and the scribes of Jeremiah chapter 36 begin to tear up the word. (Being ignorant of the two main problems of the text, they produce a tangled knot of nonsense that a saltwater fisherman could not untie.)]{.class_s1SU}

In the first place, "kept him safe" is NOT twentieth-century English, or even nineteenth-century English. You haven't heard anyone use that expression in speech for 200 years, [and you know it. ]{.class_s1SV-0}There is "cool him off," "keep him out of trouble," "put him away," "put him in the lockup," etc. (See [Bible Believer's Commentary on Genesis]{.class_s1SV-0}, Gen. 39--40), but "kept him safe" implies protection, not [incarceration]{.class_s1SV-0}.

In the second place, the word ["observe"]{.class_s1SW-0} matches [". . . and when he heard him, he did many things, and heard him gladly"]{.class_s1SW-0} (Mark 6:20). To prove to the "revisers" that they don't know what they are doing, the Lord turns them loose and they come up with this mess, ["So he protected John,"]{.class_s1SV-0}[]{#cYJ.xhtml_a25N .class-0}[\[411\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2G8){.class_s1UE .noteref} ["So he kept him in custody."]{.class_s1SV-0}[]{#cYJ.xhtml_a2AF .class-0}[\[412\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a2G9){.class_s1UE .noteref} Well, did he do ONE or [both?]{.class_s1SV-0} If he did [both]{.class_s1SV-0}, are they not both found in the [AV ]{.class_s1SV-0}1611 text, in verses 17, 19, and 20? ["And bound him in prison . . . and would have killed him; but she could not: for Herod feared John . . . ."]{.class_s1SW-0} What did the new "updating" do for the text that God hadn't already done for it 350 years ago?

The word "prevent" should be "to go ahead of" (or as one writer objects, ["prevented him"]{.class_s1SW-0} in Matthew 17:25 should be, "spoke first to him"). Well, what does the word "prevent" mean as it stands? PRE-EVENT. Is God responsible for English people forgetting what their words mean after He has given them a book in "the King's English"? When did ["pre-event"]{.class_s1SV-0} mean anything but something that happened before something else?

Couldn't you have gotten this if you had looked at the word?

Did you look at the word?

[Should it really be changed to "spoke first to him"? If so, what in the ever-lovin'-blue-eyed-world is ]{.class_s1SU}[this reading?]{.class_s1SV-1}[ "When Jesus reached home---he got there ahead of Simon---he asked him . . . ."]{.class_s1SU}[]{#cYJ.xhtml_a2GU}[\[413\]](#c1A0.xhtml_a21F){.class_s1SX .noteref}[ Did Jesus "forestall" Peter, "anticipate" Peter, "speak ahead of" Peter, or just what?
